Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sale of Umm Walad and Validity of Judge's Ruling
Intra-Hanafi dispute on enforceability of a judge's ruling regarding sale of umm walad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the enforceability of a judge's ruling to sell an umm walad and evaluate the basis of each position.

Core Idea
A later consensus does not necessarily erase an earlier valid ikhtilaf; the Hanafi school internally differs on this principle.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a critical example in the theory of qada: a judge's ruling that contradicts a later consensus. Specifically, the case of selling an umm walad (a slave mother) highlights an intra-Hanafi dispute. The dispute turns on whether the ijma' of the Tabi'een can override an earlier established difference of opinion. We will analyze the positions of Muhammad al-Shaybani versus the Two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and understand the underlying legal principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling under dispute and the claimed ijma
The judge's ruling permits the sale of an umm walad. The Tabi'een had consensus that such a sale is impermissible. Understand that this consensus is the basis of the dispute.
The consensus is not about the judge's authority but the substantive ruling.
2
State the two intra-Hanafi positions
Muhammad holds that the judge's ruling is invalid because it contradicts the ijma of the Tabi'een. The Two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the ruling is valid and enforceable.
Both positions are attributed to major Hanafi authorities.
3
Identify the underlying usul principle
The key principle is whether a later consensus (ijma' muta'akhkhir) can remove a prior established difference of opinion (ikhtilaf). The Two say no; Muhammad says yes.
This principle affects many areas of fiqh, not just this case.
4
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a judge rules to sell an umm walad, Muhammad's view renders the ruling void and unenforceable, whereas the Two's view deems it valid and enforceable.
This difference is critical for the judiciary.
5
Note the supporting authorities
Al-Khassaf in Al-Hidayah derived this from the principle that only differences of the first generation (al-sadr al-awwal) are considered. Al-Khulasa also notes a related issue about meat without tasmiyah.
These sources show how the principle is applied across different cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثال القضاء المخالف للإجماع القضاء ببيع أمهات الأولاد، والمراد من الإجماع ما ليس فيه خلاف يستند إلى دليل شرعي ومن الغريب ما في الخلاصة وأما القضاء بحل متروك التسمية عامداً فجائز عندهما وعند أبي يوسف لا يجوز ا هـ. وهو يدل على أنه مما يسوغ فيه الاجتهاد عندهما لأنه يفيد الحل كما فهمه ابن الهمام لأنه لا خلاف عندنا في عدم الحل، من قبيل ما لا يسوغ فيه الاجتهاد عندنا لنقل الفقهاء والأصوليين بحيث شددوا النكير على الشافعي في القول بحله حتى قال الأصوليون: إنه جهل لا يصلح عذراً لمخالفته الدليل القطعي. وقد ألفت فيها رسالة مشتملة على بيان الدلائل من الجانبين. وفي الهداية : المعتبر الاختلاف في الصدر الأول وهم الصحابة والتابعون وعليه فرع الخصاف أن للقاضي ببيع أم الولد لمخالفته لإجماع التابعين. وقد حكى فيه الخلاف عندنا فقيل هذا قول محمد، أما على قولهما فيجوز قضاؤه وهو مبني على أن الإجماع المتأخر هل يرفع الخلاف المتقدم؛ فعندهما لا يرفع وعنده يرفع.
And an example of a judgment contrary to consensus is a judgment to sell mothers of children. What is meant by consensus is that which has no difference of opinion based on a legal proof. And among the strange things is what is in Al-Khulasa: 'As for the judgment permitting meat left without mentioning the name of Allah deliberately, it is permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) but according to Abu Yusuf it is not permissible.' This indicates that it is subject to ijtihad according to them because it brings about permissibility as understood by Ibn al-Humam, because there is no disagreement among us regarding its impermissibility; it is from the type of what does not allow ijtihad according to us, due to the transmission of the jurists and usuliyyun to the extent that they severely censured al-Shafi'i for his opinion of its permissibility, to the point that the usuliyyun said: 'It is ignorance that cannot be an excuse for contradicting decisive evidence.' And I have written a treatise on this containing the proofs from both sides. And in Al-Hidayah: 'Considered is the difference in the first generation, meaning the Companions and the Tabi'een. On this basis, Al-Khassaf derived that the judge (may not) sell a mother of a child because it contradicts the consensus of the Tabi'een.' And he narrated the difference among us: it is said this is the opinion of Muhammad. As for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa), his judgment is permissible, and it is based on whether a later consensus can remove a prior difference; according to them it does not remove, and according to him it does remove.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage discusses the example of a ruling that contradicts ijma (consensus): a judge permitting the sale of an umm walad (a slave woman who has borne her master a child). According to the Hanafi school, the Tabi'een (the generation after the Companions) had consensus that such a sale is not allowed because the mother of a child becomes umm walad and cannot be sold. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a judge's ruling permitting such a sale is enforceable. The text references Al-Khulasa and Al-Hidayah. The key issue is whether the existence of an earlier valid ikhtilaf (difference) prevents the later consensus from being considered binding. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), a later consensus does not override an earlier established difference, so a judge can rule based on the earlier ikhtilaf. But according to Muhammad (some reports), it does override, so the ruling would be invalid. The text also notes that the issue of meat without tasmiyah is subject to ijtihad, but it is mentioned as an aside. The passage ultimately shows the complexity of determining which rulings are subject to ijtihad and whether a judge's decision can be enforced.

Key Terms
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, thereby gaining certain rights and cannot be sold.
الصدر الأول (al-sadr al-awwal): The first generation of Muslims, including the Companions and the Tabi'een.
الإجماع المتأخر (al-ijma' al-muta'akhkhir): A consensus that arises later in time, after an earlier difference of opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Muhammad's view that a judge cannot rule to sell an umm walad?
A) The Quranic verse on inheritance.
B) The consensus of the Tabi'een that such a sale is not allowed.
C) A hadith from the Prophet.
D) The opinion of Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school internally differs on whether a later consensus removes an earlier ikhtilaf; this affects the enforceability of a judge's ruling.

Qada — Judiciary

Enforcement of a Previous Judgment: Conditions and the Role of Ikhtilaf
Explaining conditions for a qadi to enforce a prior judgment and the role of ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a second qadi to enforce a previous judgment and explain the dispute over whether later ikhtilaf is considered.

Core Idea
A second qadi must enforce a prior valid judgment unless it contradicts definitive texts, but whether later ikhtilaf counts is debated.

A qadi's ruling does not exist in isolation; it may travel to another jurisdiction. When a second qadi is asked to enforce it, complex questions arise: is he bound by his own ijtihad or obligated to respect the first? This lesson examines the Hanafi rules and the internal debate over which disagreements qualify.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule from al-Quduri
Identify the four exceptions to enforcement: contradiction with Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', or an unsupported opinion.
These are the hard limits.
2
Add the nuance from Al-Jami' al-Saghir
Note the additional condition: the first qadi must be aware of the ikhtilaf on the issue. Enforcement is general even if the second qadi disagrees.
This raises the importance of the first qadi's knowledge.
3
Distinguish early vs. later ikhtilaf
The dominant Hanafi position considers only ikhtilaf of the Companions and Followers as making a case ijtihadi. Later differences (e.g., Malik, Shafi'i) are typically not sufficient.
Al-Hidayah explicitly says 'the considered difference is that of the early period.'
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Muhammad holds that later consensus overrides earlier ikhtilaf; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in another view disagree. This affects enforcement of judgments on umm walad and similar cases.
The debate hinges on whether ijma' muta'akhir removes earlier khilaf.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that a second qadi enforces unless the judgment contradicts a definitive text, regardless of his own view, provided the first qadi was qualified.
Fath al-Qadir questions the dismissal of later ikhtilaf, but the majority adheres to the early-period criterion.

That he annuls the judgment. The Book of Transfer / Chapter on the Letter of a Judge to Another Judge, etc. The censure of al-Shafi'i in saying it is permissible, such that the specialists in legal theory said: It is ignorance that does not constitute an excuse for opposing definitive evidence. And a treatise has been written on it containing clarification of proofs from both sides. In al-Hidaya: The considered [difference] is the difference in the early period—they are the Companions and the Followers—and upon it al-Khassaf branched that the judge [may sell] the mother of children because of opposing the consensus of the Followers. And the difference has been related among us: it is said this is the view of Muhammad; as for the view of both [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], his judgment is permissible, and it is based on whether later consensus removes earlier difference; in their view it does not remove, and in his view it does. In al-Taqwim of Abu Zayd that Muhammad narrated from them that judgment to sell the mother of children is not permissible. And branching from the condition that difference in the early period is a condition for the matter being subject to ijtihad, some said that the judge may nullify what the Maliki and Shafi'i have judged by his opinion. In al-Aqdiya, our companions did not consider the difference of Malik and al-Shafi'i. In Fath al-Qadir: In my view this is not reliable; if it is established that Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Abu Hanifa are mujtahids, then there is no doubt that the matter is subject to ijtihad; otherwise no, and there is no doubt that they are people of ijtihad and high rank. We indeed see in the midst of masail that a matter is made subject to ijtihad due to difference among the mashayikh so that judgment is enforced according to one of the two views; so how could it not be so when the difference is not known except among these imams? That is supported by what is in al-Dhakhira from al-Halwani: If a father effects khul' for a minor girl with her dower and sees it as good for her, such that she cannot get along with her husband, then according to Malik's view the dower leaves her ownership and the husband is absolved of it; if a judge so judges, it is enforced. And in Hayd of Minhaj al-Shari'a from Malik concerning a woman who is divorced and six months pass without menstruation: she observes a waiting period of three months afterward; if a judge so judges, it should be enforced because it is subject to ijtihad, except that something similar was transmitted from Ibn Umar who said: This mas'ala must be memorized, for it frequently occurs. That is also supported by what is in al-Khulasa: If he judged concerning a ma'dhun in one type that he is not ma'dhun in all types, it is enforced. That is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i. It is valid as being of the type in which ijtihad is not permissible according to us. Ibn Amir Hajj mentioned in his commentary on al-Tahrir, in the investigation of ignorance at the end of the book, a good discussion in this place, saying: then one may object that the matter subject to ijtihad which contradicts the indications of these three principles, which is judged to be disregarded so that judgment by it is not enforced: either it contradicts what is from the Book that is definitive in indication and not abrogated, or what is from the Sunna likewise mutawatir in transmission, or what is from the consensus that is definitive in transmission and indication—this is unquestionable, but that such a matter would issue from a mujtahid is unlikely because deeming it permissible to oppose each of those is disbelief, so it should not be the intended meaning. Or it contradicts what is from the Book or Sunna that is probable in indication, whether the Sunna is definitive in transmission or not, and from consensus what is probable in transmission or indication. This regarding the non-enforcement of a judgment opposing it is absolutely apparent until he said: What appears is that the judgment declaring permissible [marriage] while intentionally omitting the recitation of the basmalah, and [judgment] by one witness and the oath of the plaintiff, is enforced without needing approval of another judge; [judgment concerning] mothers of children is not enforced unless another judge approves it. And sale [of the mother of children]? The Book of Transfer, Chapter on the Letter of a Judge to Another Judge, etc., page 21. And the summary is that their statements have varied in this chapter: sometimes they considered their difference, other times they did not. It may be said that they only said it is enforced in these cases due to a difference preceding Malik and al-Shafi'i, not specifically due to their difference. Then know that the author of al-Hidaya first narrated the statement of al-Quduri: When a judgment of a judge is brought to him, he enforces it unless it contradicts the Book, the Sunna, or Ijma', or is an unsupported opinion. Second, what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Whatever the jurists differ about, and a judge judged it, then another judge comes who holds a different view, he enforces it. The commentators said: He only mentioned the statement of al-Jami' after al-Quduri for two benefits not in al-Quduri: first, its restriction to the jurists, so it indicates that if he [the first judge] was not aware of the difference, it is not enforced; second, the restriction that the second judge holds a different view, for al-Quduri did not address that, so it could be that his intention was that if his view agrees with the first judgment, he enforces it; if it disagrees, he does not enforce it. The narration of al-Jami' clarifies that enforcement is general except for the exceptions, whether it agrees with his view or not. And in Fath al-Qadir they criticized this, saying there is no indication in the statement of al-Jami' that he [the first judge] was aware of the difference; rather, its import is that whatever the jurists actually differed about, and the judge judged that which is differed about—aware that it is differed about or not—is general, then another judge comes who holds a different view from the one judged, he enforces it. So perhaps it indicates that the second is aware of the difference, but the discussion is not about him; it is about the first judge whose judgment is being enforced. There is no evidence that he was aware of the difference by any means of indication. Yes, in al-Jami' al-Saghir there is explicit text that he enforces it even if it is contrary to his view, and al-Quduri's statement also indicates that, for he said: When a judgment of a judge is brought to him—it is general, encompassing both the case where it is contrary to his view and where it agrees. That is it. His words: (And the summary is that their statements have become confused, etc.) Al-Ramli said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: After narrating what indicated confusion, it appears that there is a difference among our mashayikh. His words: (Then know, etc.) is repeated with what came before? Yes, in Busita? as we said. His words: (The import is that whatever the jurists differed about, etc.) The relative pronoun 'ma' is the noun of 'inna', 'ikhtalafa' is the relative clause, 'faqada' is coordinated with it, and his saying 'fa innahu a'mmu' is a justification for the generalization by his saying 'aliman aw la'. His saying 'thumma ja'a' is coordinated with 'qada', and the reference by 'hadha' is to the first judge, and his saying 'amdahu' is the predicate of 'inna', and the pronoun refers to the other judge. This, and in al-Nahr he summarized the statement of al-Fath, then said: It is confirmed in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya, but I see a problem in that: the reason that led the mashayikh to interpret Muhammad's statement to require the judge to be aware of the difference is that even if he judged a matter subject to ijtihad without knowing it, his judgment is not valid according to most of them, nor does the second enforce it, as in al-Sharh and others. It is asserted in Munyat al-Mufti: If he judged on a matter subject to ijtihad without knowing it, it is not enforced. For in al-Siyar al-Kabir: A man had mudabbars who would be freed upon his death; then another man proved a debt against him, and the judge sold them thinking they were ordinary slaves and judged it permissible; then it became clear they were mudabbars, his judgment was nullified due to his ignorance of that. Had he known and ijtihad and invalidated the tadbir, it would be permissible. So his statement 'and whatever is differed about'...
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the ruling regarding the enforcement of a previous judgment by a second qadi. The author begins by mentioning the criticism of Imam al-Shafi'i's position that such enforcement is always permissible, noting that some usuli scholars consider this ignorance that does not excuse contradicting definitive evidence. The passage then presents the view from Al-Hidayah that the ikhtilaf (disagreement) that matters is that of the early generations (Companions and Followers). Based on this, al-Khassaf ruled that a qadi may sell a mother of children (umm al-walad) because the Followers had consensus that it is impermissible, but there is ikhtilaf among earlier authorities. The passage then discusses a disagreement within the Hanafi school: Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds that if a later consensus emerges, it overrides earlier ikhtilaf, so a judgment based on the earlier view is invalid; whereas Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (in one report) hold that later consensus does not remove earlier ikhtilaf, so the judgment stands. This is termed 'al-ijma' al-muta'akhir' (later consensus). Subsequently, the passage examines whether the ikhtilaf of later imams like Malik and al-Shafi'i is considered for making a case ijtihadi. Some scholars say no, because their ikhtilaf is not from the early period. But the author of Fath al-Qadir criticizes this, arguing that if Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Abu Hanifa are all mujtahids, their ikhtilaf should render a case ijtihadi. The author supports this with examples from al-Dhakhira and al-Khulasa where judgments based on Malik's or al-Shafi'i's views are enforced. The passage then transitions to explaining the conditions for a second qadi to enforce a previous judgment. It quotes al-Quduri: the second qadi enforces unless the judgment contradicts Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', or is an unsupported opinion. Then it quotes Al-Jami' al-Saghir: if jurists differ on an issue and a qadi judges it, another qadi who holds a different view must enforce it. The commentators note that Al-Jami' adds two conditions not in al-Quduri: (1) the first qadi must be aware of the ikhtilaf, and (2) the second qadi may differ in view. However, Fath al-Qadir argues that Al-Jami' does not explicitly require the first qadi to know the ikhtilaf; it only says 'whatever the jurists actually differed about' (fi nafs al-amr), which is an objective fact. The passage concludes by noting confusion among later Hanafi scholars on this point.

Key Terms
نفاذ (nafadh): Enforcement or execution of a qadi's judgment by another qadi or authority.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): The process of independent legal reasoning by a qualified jurist to derive a ruling from the sources.
خلاف (ikhtilaf): Disagreement among jurists on a legal ruling; its existence can make a case ijtihadi and thus allow enforcement of differing judgments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when must a second qadi NOT enforce a previous judgment?
A) When the first qadi was not aware of the ikhtilaf.
B) When the judgment contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma'.
C) When the judgment is based on the ikhtilaf of later imams like Malik and Shafi'i.
D) When the second qadi holds a different view on the matter.

Key Takeaway
A second qadi must enforce a prior judgment unless it contradicts a definitive text or is a baseless opinion; the scope of enforceable ikhtilaf is limited to the early period in the dominant Hanafi view.

Qada — Judiciary
advanced
8 min
Enforcement of Prior Judgments in Disputed Matters: The Hanafi Position
Critical refinement of enforcement conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on enforcement of prior judgments, distinguish the al-Quduri and al-Jami' versions, and apply the mufta bihi position to determine enforceability in a given scenario.

Core Idea
A prior judge's ruling is enforced unless it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or is unsupported; knowledge of ikhtilaf is not required.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq tackles a critical procedural question in Islamic judiciary: when must a judge enforce the ruling of a previous judge? The Hanafi school has two main textual formulations—one from al-Quduri with explicit exceptions, and a broader one from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' that seems unconditional. The commentator resolves the apparent conflict by harmonizing them into a practical fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two source texts
Note al-Quduri's statement (enforcement with exceptions) and al-Jami' al-Saghir (general enforcement without mention of exceptions). Observe their apparent difference.
Al-Quduri: 'unless it contradicts the Book, Sunnah, Ijma, or is an unsupported opinion.' Al-Jami': 'what the jurists differed about, if a judge ruled, then another judge who disagrees enforces it.'
2
Understand the commentators' interpretation
The commentators attempted to reconcile by conditioning enforcement on the first judge's knowledge of ikhtilaf and restricting to cases where the second judge holds a different view.
They read 'jurists' in al-Jami' as implying the judge knows they differ.
3
Analyze Ibn al-Humam's objection
Ibn al-Humam (Fath al-Qadir) argued that al-Jami' does not state the first judge's knowledge; the phrase is about the issue itself. Enforcement is general
The objection shifts focus from the judge's knowledge to the nature of the dispute.
4
Recognize the author's resolution and the mufta bihi
The author (Ibn Nujaym) sides with al-Quduri's version combined with al-Khassaf's details. The fatwa: enforcement is conditional only on not contradicting clear texts and not falling under the enumerated void cases.
Quotes al-Waqi'at al-Hussamiyya and Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi: 'Muhammad's narration that enforcement is general; we take it.'
5
Memorize the specific void cases
The passage lists cases where a ruling is not enforced: e.g., dismissal due to passage of years, separation for non-payment of absent husband, marriage with adulteress, mut'a marriage, dropping mahr without evidence.
These come from al-Khassaf's Sharh Adab al-Qadi.

والحاصل أن كلامهم قد اضطرب في هذا الباب فتارة اعتبروا خلافهما، وأخرى لم يعتبروه . ويمكن أن يقال: إنهم إنما قالوا بالنفاذ في هذه المسائل لأجل خلاف سابق على مالك والشافعي لا بخلافهما خاصة. ثم اعلم أن باعتبار خلافهما اعتمد ما في الجامع. وهذا لم أسبق إليه وإنما رأيت في الواقعات الحسامية ما يفيده قال قال الفقيه أبو الليث : رواية محمد أن كل شيء اختلف فيه الفقهاء فقضى القاضي بذلك جاز قضاؤه ولم يكن لقاض خاصمته يبطل حقها في الصداق والقاضي لا يلتفت إلى خصومتها : شرح أدب القضاء
The summary is that their statements have become confused in this chapter: sometimes they considered their disagreement, and sometimes they did not. And it can be said that they only said enforcement in these issues because of a prior disagreement with Malik and al-Shafi'i, not specifically with the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Then know that the author of al-Hidayah first quoted al-Quduri's statement: 'If a judge's ruling is presented to him, he enforces it unless it contradicts the Book, the Sunnah, or consensus, or is an unsupported opinion.' And second, what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'What the jurists differed about, if a judge ruled on it, then another judge who holds a different view comes, he enforces it.' The commentators said that he mentioned the phrase of al-Jami' after al-Quduri for two benefits not in al-Quduri: one is its restriction to 'jurists,' indicating that if he was not aware of the disagreement, it is not enforced; the second is the restriction that the judge holds a different view, for al-Quduri did not address that, so it might be understood that if his view agrees with the first ruling, he enforces it, and if it contradicts, he does not. The narration of al-Jami' shows that enforcement is general except for the exceptions, whether it agrees with his view or not. Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir objected: there is no indication in the phrase of al-Jami' that he was aware of the disagreement; rather, its meaning is that what the jurists actually differed about, the judge ruled on that which they differed about, whether he was aware or not, then another judge comes who holds a different view from that which this judge ruled, he enforces it. Perhaps it indicates that the second is aware of the disagreement, but the discussion is not about him; rather it is about the first judge whose ruling is enforced. And there is no evidence that he was aware of the disagreement by any mode of indication. Yes, in al-Jami' al-Saghir there is explicit text that he enforces it even if it contradicts his view, and al-Quduri's statement also indicates it, for he said: 'If a judge's ruling is presented to him,' which is general and includes both contradictory and agreeable. End. This is it: His statement: (The summary is that their statements have become confused, etc.) al-Ramli said in Jami' al-Fusulayn after quoting what necessitates confusion: it appears that there is a disagreement among our scholars. His statement: (Then know, etc.) is repeated with what preceded. Yes, in Basuta based on what preceded. His statement: (And its meaning is that what the jurists differed about) 'what' is the relative noun of 'inna,' and 'differed' is the relative clause, and his statement 'and ruled' is coordinated with it, and his statement 'for it is general' etc. is a justification for generalization by his saying 'aware or not.' And his statement 'then comes' is coordinated with 'ruled,' and the reference in his statement 'this' is to the first judge, and his statement 'he enforces it' is the predicate of 'inna,' and the pronoun in it refers to the other judge. This and the statement in al-Nahr summarizing al-Fath's words, then he said: and he approved it in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya, but I have a reservation: the reason for the scholars to interpret Muhammad's statement as requiring that the judge be aware of the disagreement is that if he ruled in a matter of ijtihad without knowing that, his ruling is not permissible according to the majority, and the second does not enforce it as in the commentary and others. It is determined in Munyat al-Mufti where he said: 'He ruled in a matter of ijtihad without knowing it, it is not enforced.' For it is mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir: 'He had tadbirs who were freed upon his death. A man established a debt against him, so the judge sold them assuming they were slaves and ruled its permissibility. Then it appeared they were mudabbars; his ruling was annulled due to his lack of knowledge. Had he known and made ijtihad and invalidated the tadbir, it would have been permissible.' End. So his statement 'and what the jurists differed about' said 'who?' and I say: they did not understand the intent of the author of al-Hidayah: that he mentioned the phrase of al-Jami' after al-Quduri to indicate that what is in al-Jami' has no exception; rather, every issue the jurists differed about becomes a subject of ijtihad. If a judge rules by an opinion, the disagreement is resolved. As for al-Quduri's phrase, it has exceptions as you know. Once you know that, what the fatwa authors mentioned of cases where a judge's ruling is not enforced due to contradiction with the Book, famous Sunnah, or consensus, is only according to al-Quduri's phrase. As for according to what is in al-Jami', it is not. And you know from this that no consideration is given to the disagreement of Malik and al-Shafi'i; those who rely on al-Quduri's statement do not consider it, and those who say consideration is given to their disagreement rely on al-Jami'. This has not been preceded by me, but I saw in al-Waqi'at al-Hussamiyya what indicates it: al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: 'Muhammad's narration is that everything the jurists differed about, if a judge ruled on it, his ruling is valid, and no other judge may nullify it; and he did not mention the disagreement, and we take it.' I say: this contradicts what is mentioned in Sharh Adab al-Qadi attributed to al-Khassaf: that ruling in a place of disagreement is permissible, and in a place of disagreement is not permissible. He meant by the first what has a valid disagreement like the disagreement among the Salaf, and by 'place of disagreement' what is not considered valid, and he did not consider the disagreement of al-Shafi'i. He said: 'The fatwa is on the details of Adab al-Qadi.' End. So this statement removed confusion and clarified all speculation and conjecture. The summary is that the fatwa is on the statement of al-Quduri and the details of al-Khassaf. For this reason, the author of al-Hidayah mentioned what is in al-Jami' after al-Quduri. Now we will mention the places where the scholars of the school have explicitly stated cases where the judge's ruling is not enforced, taken from the words of al-Khassaf, and we have mentioned them in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyya, and it is good to list them here to complete the benefit. He ruled the dismissal of a case due to passage of years, or separated between spouses due to inability to pay maintenance while absent, or ruled the validity of marriage with the father's or son's adulteress, or the validity of marriage with the mother or daughter of one's adulteress, or the validity of mut'a marriage, or the dropping of the mahr without evidence or acknowledgment based on someone's statement that the prior marriage causes the dropping of mahr, or without deferment. His statement: (Or the dropping of the mahr) its scenario is that if a woman does not dispute with her husband regarding the prescribed (mahr) until a long period passes, then she disputes, her right to the dower is annulled, and the judge does not pay attention to her dispute: Sharh Adab al-Qadi.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement by the commentator of al-Bahr al-Raiq, Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, addressing a dispute among Hanafi scholars about the conditions under which a judge's ruling must be enforced by a subsequent judge. The discussion centers on two key texts: al-Quduri's statement in al-Mukhtasar, which says a judge enforces another's ruling unless it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or is an unsupported opinion; and al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad, which says that in matters where jurists differ, if a judge rules, another judge who holds a different view must enforce it. At first glance, al-Jami' appears more permissive—no exceptions—while al-Quduri lists exceptions. The commentators tried to reconcile them by saying al-Jami' adds two conditions: first, the first judge must be aware of the disagreement (because 'jurists' implies he knows they differ); second, the second judge must hold a different view. Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir refuted this: al-Jami' does not state the first judge's awareness; it simply says 'what the jurists differed about' in reality. Thus, enforcement is general whether the first judge knew or not. The only condition is that the second judge sees differently. The commentator then presents his own view: al-Hidayah cited al-Jami' after al-Quduri to show that al-Jami' has no exceptions—any disputed issue becomes amenable to ijtihad, so a judge's ruling resolves it. Al-Quduri, by contrast, retains exceptions. Therefore, the fatwa is based on al-Quduri's version and the detailed work of al-Khassaf (Adab al-Qadi). The commentator then lists several cases where a judge's ruling is not enforced: dismissing a case due to lapse of time, separating spouses for non-payment of maintenance while the husband is absent, validating marriage with a relative's adulteress, mut'a marriage, dropping mahr without evidence, etc. The practical result: a judge must be careful; rulings that go against clear texts or established principles are void.

Key Terms
خلاف معتبر (khilaf mu'tabar): A disagreement among jurists that is considered valid and worthy of consideration, such as the disagreements of the Salaf (early scholars).
موضع الاختلاف (mawdi' al-ikhtilaf): A matter where there is a valid, recognized disagreement among qualified jurists.
نفاذ (nafadh): The enforceability or execution of a judge's ruling; it is binding on other judges under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in this passage, what is the basis for a judge's ruling being enforceable by another judge?
A) The ruling must be based on the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, and must not be an unsupported opinion.
B) The first judge must have been aware of the disagreement among jurists.
C) The second judge must hold the same opinion as the first.
D) The ruling must be on a matter not mentioned in al-Quduri's exceptions.

Key Takeaway
Enforcement of prior judgments in the Hanafi school is wajib and unconditional except when the ruling violates explicit textual sources or falls into the specific void cases enumerated by al-Khassaf.

Qada — Judiciary

The Principle: When a Judge's Ruling is Final or Void
Clarifying the foundational rule on enforceability of judgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions (Al-Quduri and Al-Jami') regarding enforceability of judgments in disputed matters and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling in recognized ikhtilaf is final; if it contradicts clear nass, it is void.

The passage begins by clarifying a key confusion: the author of Al-Hidayah mentions Al-Jami' after Al-Quduri to indicate that every ijtihadable matter is open to interpretation, but Al-Quduri's statement carves out an exception for rulings that directly contradict the Quran, well-known Sunnah, or Ijma. This lesson unpacks that distinction and shows how it determines whether a judgment can be overturned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting statements
Find the statements from Al-Jami' (every difference becomes subject to ijtihad, judgment final) and from Al-Quduri (exception for rulings contradicting clear texts).
The core of the dispute is whether any ruling in a disputed area is automatically final.
2
Understand the resolution
The fatwa rests on Al-Quduri's exception and al-Khassaf's detail: judgments in recognized ikhtilaf (مَوْضِعُ الِاخْتِلَاف) are final, but judgments in unrecognized disagreement (مَوْضِعُ الْخِلَاف) that contradict clear evidence are not.
Recognized ikhtilaf includes disagreements among the Salaf; unrecognized includes opinions like those of Malik or al-Shafi'i when contrary to established nass.
3
Apply the rule
Given a hypothetical judgment, determine if it falls under recognized ikhtilaf (final) or contradicts clear texts (void).
This is the practical skill for a qadi or mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأقول : لم يفهموا مراد صاحب الهداية أنما ذكر عبارة الجامع بعد القدوري ليفيد أن ما في الجامع لا استثناء فيه بل كل مسألة اختلفت فيها الفقهاء فإنها تصير محل اجتهاد، فإن قضى قاض بقول ارتفع الخلاف، وأما عبارة القدوري فاستثناء كما علمت. وإذا علمت ذلك فما ذكره أصحاب الفتاوى من المسائل التي لا ينفذ فيها قضاء القاضي لمخالفة كتاب أو سنة مشهورة أو إجماع إنما هو على عبارة القدوري، وأما على ما في الجامع فلا. وعلمت من هنا أن لا اعتبار بخلاف مالك والشافعي اعتمد قول القدوري، ومن قال باعتبار خلافهما اعتمد ما في الجامع. وهذا لم أسبق إليه وإنما رأيت في الواقعات الحسامية ما يفيده قال قال الفقيه أبو الليث : رواية محمد أن كل شيء اختلف فيه الفقهاء فقضى القاضي بذلك جاز قضاؤه ولم يكن لقاض آخر أن يبطله ولم يذكر فيه الاختلاف وبه نأخذ قلت هذا خلاف ما ذكره في شرح أدب القاضي المنسوب إلى الخصاف أن القضاء في موضع الاختلاف يجوز، وفي موضع الخلاف لا يجوز . أراد بالأوّل ما كان فيه خلاف معتبر كالخلاف بين السلف وأراد بموضع الخلاف ما لم يكن معتبراً ولم يعتبر بخلاف الشافعي . قال أستأذنا : الفتوى على تفاصيل أدب القاضي ا هـ . فهذه العبارة أزالت اللبس وأوضحت كل تخمين وحدس والحاصل أن الفتوى على عبارة القدوري وتفاصيل الخصاف فلهذا السر أورد صاحب الهداية ما في الجامع بعد القدوري، فالآن نذكر المواضع التي نص أهل المذهب على مسائل لا ينفذ القضاء فيها أخذاً من كلام الخصاف وقد ذكرناها في الفوائد الفقهية ولا بأس بسردها تكميلاً للفائدة هنا . قضى ببطلان الدعوى بمضي سنين، أو فرق بين الزوجين لعجزه عن النفقة حال غيبته، أو حكم بصحة نكاح مزنية أبيه أو ابنه أو بصحة نكاح أم مزنيته أو بنتها، أو بصحة نكاح المتعة أو بسقوط المهر بلا بينة أو إقرار أخذاً بقول البعض، إن قدم النكاح يوجب سقوط المهر، أو بعدم تأجيل العنين، أو بعدم صحة الرجعة بلا رضاها، أو بعدم وقوع الثلاث على الحامل، أو بعدم وقوع الثلاث على غير المدخولة، أو بعدم وقوع الطلاق في طهر جامعها فيه، أو بنصف الجهاز لمن طلق امرأته قبل الدخول بها بعد قبض المهر والتجهيز أو بالشهادة على خط أبيه أو بشاهد ويمين، أو في الحدود والقصاص بشهادة رجل أو امرأتين أو بما في ديوانه، وقد نسي وبشهادة شاهد على صك لم يذكر ما فيه إلا أنه يعرف خطه وخاتمه أو بشهادة من شهد على قضية مختومة من غير أن تقرأ عليه، وبقضاء المرأة في حد وقود بقضاء عبد أو أو نصراني، أو في قسامة بقتل، أو فرق بين الزوجين بشهادة واحدة على الرضاع أو قضى لولده بشهادة الأجانب أو حكم بالحجر على مفسد مستحق له أو بصحة بيع نصيب الساكت من قن حرره أحد الشريكين معسراً. وبجواز متروك التسمية عامداً، أو بجواز بيع أم الولد أو ببطلان. بيع صبي
I say: They did not understand the intent of the author of Al-Hidayah: he only mentioned the statement of Al-Jami‘ after Al-Quduri to indicate that what is in Al-Jami‘ has no exception, rather every matter in which the jurists differed becomes a subject of ijtihad. If a judge passes judgment according to a position, the disagreement ceases. As for the statement of Al-Quduri, it is exceptional as you know. Now that you know this, what the authors of fatwas mentioned regarding cases where the judgment of a judge is not executed due to contradiction with the Book, well-known Sunnah, or consensus is based on Al-Quduri’s statement. As for what is in Al-Jami‘, that is not the case. From this you know that the positions of Malik and al-Shafi‘i are not considered. Whoever relied on Al-Quduri, and whoever said their disagreement is considered relied on what is in Al-Jami‘. I have not come across this before; I only saw in Al-Waqi‘at al-Husamiyyah something that indicates it: al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: Muhammad’s narration is that everything about which the jurists differed, if a judge passes judgment accordingly, his judgment is valid and no other judge may nullify it. He did not mention the disagreement. We follow this. I said: This contradicts what is mentioned in Sharh Adab al-Qadi attributed to al-Khassaf: that judgment in a place of difference [recognized] is valid, and in a place of disagreement [unrecognized] is not valid. By the first he meant what has recognized difference like the difference among the Salaf; by 'place of disagreement' he meant what is not recognized, and he did not consider the disagreement of al-Shafi‘i. He said: our teacher: the fatwa is according to the details of Adab al-Qadi. This statement removed confusion and clarified all conjecture. The upshot is that the fatwa is according to Al-Quduri’s statement and the details of al-Khassaf. For this reason the author of Al-Hidayah brought what is in Al-Jami‘ after Al-Quduri. Now we mention the cases where the scholars of the school have stated that judgment is not executed, taken from al-Khassaf’s words. We have mentioned them in Al-Fawa’id al-Fiqhiyyah, and it is good to list them here to complete the benefit. He passed judgment that the claim is void due to passage of years; or separated the spouses due to husband’s inability to pay maintenance while absent; or ruled on the validity of marriage with the one who committed zina with his father or son, or validity of marriage with the mother or daughter of the woman with whom he committed zina, or validity of mut‘ah marriage, or dropping of the mahr without evidence or acknowledgment, taking from the statement of some that prior marriage causes the dropping of the mahr; or regarding the postponement for the impotent; or regarding the invalidity of revocation without her consent; or regarding the non-occurrence of triple divorce on a pregnant woman; or regarding the non-occurrence of triple divorce on a non-consummated woman; or regarding the non-occurrence of divorce during a period of purity in which he had intercourse; or regarding half of the trousseau for one who divorced his wife before consummation after receiving the mahr and trousseau; or regarding testimony on his father’s handwriting; or with one witness and an oath; or in hadd and qisas cases with testimony of one man or two women; or based on what is in his register while he has forgotten; or with testimony of a witness on a document without mentioning what is in it except that he recognizes his handwriting and seal; or with testimony of one who testified on a sealed case without it being read to him; or with the judgment of a woman in hadd and retaliation; or with judgment of a slave or a Christian; or regarding qasamah in killing; or separated the spouses with single testimony on suckling; or passed judgment for his child with testimony of strangers; or ruled for restriction (hajr) on a corrupt person who deserves restriction; or regarding validity of sale of the silent partner’s share of a slave emancipated by one of the partners while insolvent; or regarding permissibility of intentional omission of tasmiyah; or regarding permissibility of sale of umm al-walad; or regarding invalidity of sale of a minor.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the conditions under which a judge's ruling is enforceable. The author begins by clarifying a point of confusion regarding the statements of Al-Hidayah and Al-Quduri. The key principle is: if a judge passes a ruling in a matter where there is recognized ikhtilaf among the jurists, that ruling is generally final and cannot be overturned by another judge. However, if the ruling contradicts clear texts from the Quran, well-known Sunnah, or consensus (ijma), it is not enforceable. The author then lists numerous specific cases where qada (judgment) is not executed. These are instances where the ruling would be contrary to established textual evidence. For example, ruling that triple divorce does not occur on a pregnant woman or during menstruation contradicts the Quranic verse (2:230) and thus the ruling is void. Similarly, ruling based on testimony that violates the rules of evidence (like two women in hadd cases) is unenforceable. The list is derived from al-Khassaf's work on qada. The author notes that the fatwa is upon Al-Quduri's statement and al-Khassaf's details. This passage serves as a practical guide for judges and students, showing that not all judgments are binding if they deviate from core sources.

Key Terms
قضاء القاضي (qada' al-qadi): The official judgment issued by a judge in a legal case.
موضع الخلاف (mawdi' al-khilaf): A matter where the disagreement among jurists is not considered valid or strong enough to be relied upon.
لا ينفذ (la yunfadh): The ruling is not executed; it is null and void, and can be overturned by another judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in this passage, a judge's ruling that a woman can be divorced without her consent during her menstrual period is:
A) Enforceable because it is a matter of ikhtilaf.
B) Not enforceable because it contradicts clear hadith.
C) Enforceable only if the judge is a Hanafi.
D) Not enforceable because it is against the majority view.

Key Takeaway
A judge's ruling is only final in matters of recognized ikhtilaf; if it contradicts decisive evidence from Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma, it is void.

Specific Cases Where a Judge's Ruling Is Not Enforced
Listing specific judgments that are not enforceable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and categorize the cases where a judge's ruling is not enforceable according to the Hanafi school, based on the list from al-Khassaf.

Core Idea
Over 20 specific rulings are void because they violate the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma.

The passage now provides a comprehensive list of judgments that are void and can be overturned. These span family law, evidence, and commercial transactions. This lesson helps you recognize the common thread: each ruling contradicts a clear textual ruling. Understanding these examples equips you to identify unenforceable rulings beyond the list.

Guided Path
1
Read the list and identify categories
The examples fall under categories: marriage validity, divorce effects, evidence and testimony, penal law, etc.
Grouping helps memory and application.
2
For each example, identify the clear text it contradicts
For each, infer the specific Quranic verse, hadith, or ijma that it violates.
This builds the skill of connecting fiqh rulings to their sources.
3
Synthesize the principle
Any judgment contradicting a clear rule of fiqh is unenforceable. The list is illustrative, not exhaustive.
The qawida 'la yunfadh' governs all such cases.

Nullification of Judgments Contrary to Clear Evidence
Lists rulings that a second judge may nullify due to deviation from clear evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a judge's ruling can be nullified by another judge according to the Hanafi school, and apply the principle to the specific case of triple divorce.

Core Idea
A judgment that contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma' is void and must be overturned.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates dozens of scenarios where a second judge can nullify a first judge's ruling. The unifying principle is that any verdict deviating from clear textual evidence (nass) or consensus (ijma') carries no legal weight. We will focus on the most detailed example—triple divorce—to understand the reasoning behind nullification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is a judge's verdict in a legal dispute. Normally, judges' rulings are enforceable and final. However, when the ruling deviates from clear evidence, it loses its authority.
2
Locate the condition for nullification
The text states that a ruling is nullifiable if it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma'. The example of triple divorce shows that the Quranic verse (2:230) clearly implies three divorces are effective; any contrary ruling is void.
The condition is: the ruling must be based on a deviant opinion (qawl al-zaygh) that opposes established textual evidence.
3
Apply to the triple divorce scenario
If a judge rules that triple divorce during menstruation, pregnancy, or before consummation does not occur (or occurs as one), that ruling contradicts the Quran. A second judge must nullify it and enforce the original divorce.
The author explicitly warns against the fatwa of Ibn Kamal Pasha, which claimed one divorce occurs; such a fatwa is not reliable.
4
Distinguish between subject-matter and judgment disputes
The text differentiates between disagreement over the subject of judgment (maqdi bihi) and disagreement over the judgment itself (qada'). In the former (like triple divorce), the ruling is void; in the latter (like judgment against an absentee), the ruling requires ratification by another judge because it is a matter of ijtihad.
Example: a judge's ruling against an absent party is not automatically enforceable; it depends on another judge's ratification.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a judge rules based on a deviant opinion, the second judge must nullify it to uphold the Shari'ah. If the first ruling is in a matter of ijtihad, the second judge may either ratify or reject it, but nullification is not automatic.

قوله: (أو بعدم وقوع الثلاث على غير المدخولة) قال في المنح بعد هذا: أو بعدم وقوع طلاق الحائض أو بعدم وقوع الزائد على الواحد أو بعدم وقوع الثلاث بكلمة أو بعدم وقوع الطلاق في طهر الخ. والظاهر أن هذا سقط من الناسخ وعبارة شرح أدب القضاء أوضح وهي قوله قال : وكذلك رجل طلق زوجته ثلاثاً . حبلى أو حائض أو قبل أن يدخل بها فقضى قاض بإبطال ذلك أو أبطل بعضه فرفع إلى قاض آخر لا يرى ذلك فإنه يبطل قضاء القاضي بذلك وينفذ على الزوج ما كان منه لأن على قول أهل الزيغ إذا أوقع الثلاث وهي حبلى أو في حالة الحيض أو في طهر جامعها فيه لا يقع أصلاً، وعلى قول الحسن البصري إذا أوقع الثلاث تقع واحدة لكن كلا القولين باطل لأنه مخالف للكتاب قال الله تعالى فإن طلقها فلا تحل له من بعد ﴾ [البقرة: ۲۳۰] الآية. من غير فصل والمراد منه الطلقة الثالثة فمن قال لا يقع شيء أو تقع واحدة فقد أثبت الحل للزوج الأول بدون الزوج الثاني وهو مخالف للكتاب، فإذا قضى القاضي لا ينفذ فإذا رفع إلى قاض آخر كان له أن يبطله اهـ. أقول : وبهذا يعلم أن ما ذكر في الفتاوى المنسوبة إلى ابن كمال باشا من وقوع طلقة واحدة لو ثلاثاً وهي حائض أو حبلى أو غير مدخول بها باطل لا يعوّل عليه فتنبه قوله : (أو بالشهادة على خط أبيه صورته أن الرجل إذا مات فوجد ابنه خط أبيه في صك علم يقيناً أنه خط أبيه يشهد بذلك الصك لأن الابن خليفة الميت في جميع الأشياء؛ شرح أدب القضاء قوله : (أو في قسامة بقتل) قال الرملي : أي قضى بما فيه القسامة بالقتل .اهـ. قوله : (أو حكم بالحجر على مفسد) قال في شرح أدب القضاء : ولو أن قاضياً حجر على رجل فاسد يستحق الحجر فجاء قاض آخر فأطلق حجره وأجاز ما صنع كان إطلاقه جائزاً، وما صنع في ماله من شراء أو بيع قبل إطلاقه وبعد إطلاقه عنه جاز لوجهين: أحدهما أن الأول ليس بقضاء لعدم المقضى له والمقضى عليه بل فتوى منه فكان للثاني أن لا يعمل به فيطلق والثاني إن كان قضاء فنفس القضاء مجتهد فيه فلا يكون حجراً منه بل يتوقف على إمضاء قاض آخر إن أمضاه نفذ وصار قول القاضي. الثاني بياناً في محل مجتهد والبيان من الثاني في محل مجتهد . يكون بمنزلة القضاء في محل مجتهد ولو قضى في محل مجتهد فيه ينفذ قضاؤه ولا يكون

قوله : (أو بصحة ضمان الخلاص يريد به أن الإنسان يبيع داره من إنسان ويضمن له الخلاص أو غير البائع يضمن له الخلاص وتفسيره أنه لو جاء مستحق واستحقها فهو ضامن للخلاص يستخلص الدار من يد المستحق إما شراء أو هبة أو بوجه من الوجوه، فإذا ضمن كذلك ثم ظهر الاستحقاق فرفع إلى قاض آخر يرى ذلك الضمان صحيحاً فقضى عليه بتسليم الدار ثم رفع إلى آخر لا يراه فإنه يبطله لأنه شرط لا يقدر على الوفاء به، وهذا التفسير قول أبي حنيفة واختيار الخصاف، وأما عندهما فهو والعهدة والدرك واحد وهو الرجوع بالثمن على البائع عند الاستحقاق وتمامه في شرح أدب القضاء قوله : (أو بحد بحكم التعريض كقوله لآخر أما أنا فلست بزان قوله: (ليعم
The Book of Transfer of Debt, Chapter on the Judge's Letter to Another Judge, etc. Or (rulings such as) the impotent man, or the invalidity of revocable divorce without her consent, or the non-occurrence of triple divorce on a pregnant woman, or the non-occurrence of triple divorce on one not consummated with, or the non-occurrence of divorce during a purity in which he had intercourse, or half the trousseau for one who divorces his wife before consummation after receiving the dowry and trousseau, or on testimony on the handwriting of his father, or on a single witness and an oath, or in hudud and qisas on the testimony of one man or two women, or on what is in his register while having forgotten, or on the testimony of a witness on a document who did not mention its contents except that he knows his handwriting and seal, or on the testimony of one who testified on a sealed verdict without it being read to him, and on the judgment of a woman in a hadd, or on the judgment of a slave or a Christian, or on qasama concerning murder, or separation between spouses on the testimony of a single woman on suckling, or he judged for his child on the testimony of strangers, or he ruled on interdiction against a corrupt person who deserves it, or on the validity of the sale of the share of the silent partner from a slave freed by one of two partners while insolvent, and on the permissibility of deliberately omitting the basmala, or on the permissibility of selling an umm walad, or on the invalidity of the sale of a boy. His statement: (or the non-occurrence of triple divorce on one not consummated with) He said in al-Manh after this: or the non-occurrence of divorce of a menstruating woman, or the non-occurrence of more than one, or the non-occurrence of triple divorce with one word, or the non-occurrence of divorce during purity etc. And it seems that this was omitted by the copyist, and the expression of Sharh Adab al-Qada is clearer, which is his statement: Likewise a man divorces his wife three times while pregnant, menstruating, or before consummation; a judge rules to nullify that or nullifies part of it; then it is raised to another judge who does not hold that view — then he nullifies the judgment of the first judge and enforces against the husband what he did, because according to the deviant opinion, if he pronounces triple divorce while pregnant, menstruating, or in a purity in which he had intercourse, it does not occur at all, and according to al-Hasan al-Basri, if he pronounces triple divorce, one divorce occurs. But both statements are false because they contradict the Book. Allah said: 'Then if he divorces her, she is not lawful for him thereafter until...' [2:230] without distinction. What is meant is the third divorce. So whoever says nothing occurs or one occurs has affirmed permissibility for the first husband without the second husband, which contradicts the Book. So if a judge rules thus, it is not enforceable, and if it is raised to another judge, he may nullify it. End. I say: By this it is known that what is mentioned in the fatwas attributed to Ibn Kamal Pasha about one divorce occurring if three are pronounced while menstruating, pregnant, or unconsummated is false and not relied upon; so be warned. His statement: (or on testimony on the handwriting of his father) Its form is that if a man dies and his son finds his father's handwriting on a document and knows with certainty that it is his father's handwriting, he testifies to that document because the son is the successor of the deceased in all matters. Sharh Adab al-Qada. His statement: (or on qasama concerning murder) Al-Ramli said: meaning he ruled on what involves qasama concerning murder. His statement: (or he ruled on interdiction against a corrupt person) He said in Sharh Adab al-Qada: If a judge placed interdiction on a corrupt man who deserves interdiction, then another judge came and removed his interdiction and allowed what he did, his removal is valid, and what he did in his property of purchase or sale before his removal and after his removal from him is valid for two reasons: one is that the first was not a judgment because there was no plaintiff or defendant, but rather a fatwa from him, so it was permissible for the second not to act on it and thus remove; the second is that if it was a judgment, the judgment itself is subject to ijtihad, so it does not become an interdiction from him, but rather depends on ratification by another judge — if he ratifies it, it is enforced and becomes the word of the second judge. Explanation in a subject of ijtihad, and the explanation from the second in a subject of ijtihad is like a judgment in a subject of ijtihad. If he judges in a subject of ijtihad, his judgment is enforced and does not become... His statement: Or the woman's pardon of qisas based on the saying of some that they have no right to it, or the validity of guarantee of extrication (daman al-khalas) and he obliged him to deliver the house upon claim, or the increase in the imam's salary from mosque endowments, or the permissibility of a thrice-divorced woman through merely the contract of a tahlil without consummation, acting on the saying of Sa'id, or the non-ownership by disbelievers of the Muslim's property freed in their land, or the permissibility of selling a dirham for two dirhams, taking from the saying of Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both), or the validity of prayer of one with invalid ablution, or qasama on the people of a neighborhood for loss of property by analogy to life, or hadd of slander by way of allusion, or lottery among slaves where the deceased freed one of them, or the impermissibility of a woman's disposal of her property without her husband's permission. These issues are transmitted from al-Bazzaziyya, Jami' al-Fusulayn, al-Khaniyya, al-Quniyya, and al-Sayrafiyya. In al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir of al-Suyuti, attributed to Fatawa al-Subki, that the judgment of a judge is nullified according to the Hanafis if it is a ruling with no evidence. He said: And whatever violates the condition of the waqf violates the text, and it is a ruling with no evidence, whether the text in the waqf is clear or apparent. End. This is in agreement with the statement of our scholars like others: 'The condition of the waqf is like the text of the Lawgiver, so it must be followed' as stated in Sharh al-Majma' by the author. All this is when the disagreement is in the subject matter of the judgment. As for when it is in the judgment itself, there are two narrations: in one narration it is not enforced, mentioned by al-Khassaf, and it is the correct one, because the locus of disagreement does not exist before the judgment; when he judges, then at that time the locus of disagreement and ijtihad exists, so another judgment is needed to favor one of them. That is like judgment against an absentee and for an absentee, and the judgment of one who has been subjected to hadd for slander and his testimony after repentance. Thus mentioned the commentator. In Fath al-Qadir from the chapter on the missing person: If the judge sees the interest in judging against the absentee or for him, and he rules, it is not enforced because it is subject to ijtihad. If it is said: It should not be enforced until another judge ratifies it, because the judgment itself is subject to ijtihad, as in the case of a judge who has been subjected to hadd for slander, then the enforcement of his judgment is dependent on another judge's ratification. The answer is that it is denied that... For the second to reject it, so if the second explains, the third has no right to reject it. If the second judge rejects the first judgment, it becomes void, then the third cannot enforce it. And this is analogous to a judge who rules in an incident while he is subjected to hadd for slander; that judgment is not a proof until it is connected with ratification from the second judge. End. And you know well that our discussion is about that which is not enforced in judgment, and judgment of interdiction is not enforced as you know that it is a fatwa, but if another judge ratifies it, it is enforced. His statement: (or the validity of guarantee of extrication) He intends that a person sells his house to someone and guarantees him extrication, or someone other than the seller guarantees him extrication. Its explanation is that if a claimant comes and claims it, he is the guarantor of extrication; he extricates the house from the hand of the claimant either by purchase, gift, or any means. So if he guarantees thus, then the claim appears, and it is raised to another judge who considers that guarantee valid, so he rules against him to deliver the house; then it is raised to another who does not hold it valid, then he nullifies it because it is a condition that cannot be fulfilled. This interpretation is the view of Abu Hanifa and the choice of al-Khassaf. As for the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is the same as 'uhda and darak, which is recourse to the seller for the price upon claim. The rest is in Sharh Adab al-Qada. His statement: (or hadd by way of allusion) like saying to another: 'As for me, I am not an adulterer' – his statement: 'to generalize'.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the chapter on the judge's letter to another judge, specifically discussing cases where a second judge can nullify the ruling of a first judge. The author lists numerous scenarios where a judgment contradicts clear textual evidence (nass) or consensus, rendering it void and subject to nullification by another judge. The fundamental principle is that a judge's ruling based on a deviant opinion that opposes the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma' is not enforceable and can be overturned.

The text begins with examples such as the case of an impotent husband, the invalidity of revocable divorce without the wife's consent, and the non-occurrence of triple divorce on a pregnant woman or one not consummated with, or divorce during a period of purity in which intercourse occurred. These are all rulings against the standard Hanafi position that triple divorce is effective irrespective of these circumstances. The author emphasizes that the opinion that such divorces do not occur or occur as one is deviant (ahl al-zaygh) and contradicts the Quranic verse (2:230) which clearly implies the effectiveness of triple divorce. Therefore, if a judge rules based on that deviant view, another judge may nullify it. The author also warns against the fatwa of Ibn Kamal Pasha which claimed that triple divorce during menstruation etc. counts as one, calling it false.

Further examples include: testimony on a father's handwriting, where the son can testify based on certainty; qasama (oath-based liability) in murder cases; interdiction (hajr) on a corrupt person – here the author clarifies that the first judge's action is not a final judgment but a fatwa, so the second judge can remove it; or if considered a judgment, it requires ratification due to being a matter of ijtihad. The text discusses the distinction between disagreement in the subject matter (maqdi bihi) versus disagreement in the judgment itself (qada'). For the latter, such as judgment against an absentee or a judge who had been punished for slander, there are two narrations; the correct one is that such a judgment is not enforceable without ratification by another judge.

Other examples include: the validity of a guarantee of extrication (daman al-khalas) – interpreted differently by Abu Hanifa and the two companions; pardoning qisas by a woman based on a weak opinion; increasing the imam's salary from mosque endowments against the waqf conditions; permitting a thrice-divorced woman through a mere tahlil contract without consummation (acting on an isolated view of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab); non-ownership of Muslims' property by disbelievers in their land; selling a dirham for two dirhams (riba); validity of prayer without ablution; qasama on a neighborhood for lost property by analogy to life; hadd for slander by way of allusion; lottery among slaves; and women's disposal of property without husband's permission. The author notes these are compiled from various Hanafi fatwa collections.

The passage concludes with a key principle from al-Subki: a judgment is nullified by Hanafis if it is a ruling with no evidence. Violating the condition of a waqf is like violating the text of the Lawgiver, so it must be followed. The final section clarifies that when the disagreement is in the judgment itself (e.g., ruling against an absentee), there is a difference of opinion; the preferred view is that such a judgment does not execute without ratification by another judge. The text provides an analogy: a judge who has been subjected to hadd for slander – his judgments are not effective until ratified by another judge.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada): A judge's binding verdict in a legal dispute.
القسامة (al-qasama): An oath-based procedure for establishing liability in murder cases where there is no clear evidence.
الحجر (al-hajr): Interdiction: a legal restriction on a person's capacity to dispose of property due to reasons like bankruptcy or corruption.
ضمان الخلاص (daman al-khalas): A guarantee to extricate property from a rightful claimant by any means, distinct from simple warranty.
التعريض (al-ta'rid): An allusion or indirect statement implying slander, without explicit accusation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a judge rules that triple divorce does not occur when pronounced during menstruation?
A) The ruling is final and cannot be overturned.
B) Another judge may nullify the ruling because it contradicts the Quran.
C) The ruling is valid but the husband must repeat the divorce.
D) The matter is left to the husband's discretion.

Key Takeaway
A judge's ruling that contradicts clear textual evidence (nass) or consensus (ijma') is null and void, and a second judge must overturn it to uphold the Shari'ah.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
6 min
The Enforceability of a Judgment Against an Absent Party
Discusses enforceability of judgment against absent party

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a judgment against an absent party and explain the dispute regarding its enforcement by the same or another judge.

Core Idea
A judgment against an absent party is valid, but its enforcement is contested: must it be executed by another judge?

This passage from Ibn Nujaym's al-Bahr al-Raiq examines a critical procedural issue: can a judge pass a verdict without the defendant present? While all Hanafi authorities agree such a judgment is valid, they differ on who may enforce it. The text presents multiple views, including the position that enforcement requires another judge and the view that the same judge can enforce it. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for proper judicial procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine what the Hanafi school says about the validity of a judgment rendered without the defendant present. Note that it is considered valid (nāfidh).
2
Recognize the ikhtilaf
Notice that despite the validity, there is a disagreement on enforcement. The text says 'اختلف الترجيح' (there is disagreement on the preferred view).
3
Analyze the positions
Two positions emerge: (1) immediate enforcement by the same judge (supported by al-Khulasa and al-Islah), and (2) enforcement only by another judge (supported by Fath al-Qadir).
4
Understand the rationale
The view requiring another judge is based on the ijtihadi nature of the initial judgment — because the permissibility of judging without the absent party is itself a matter of ijtihad, execution should be handled by a different judge to avoid bias.
5
Apply the ruling
Know that in practice, the preferred view (mufta bihi) according to later authorities is that enforcement requires another judge. This has implications for how plaintiffs proceed after obtaining a default judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحوالة / باب كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي وغيره ذلك بل المجتهد سببه وهو هذه البينة هل تكون حجة للقضاء من غير خصم حاضر أم لا، فإذا قضى بها نفذ كما لو قضى بشهادة المحدود في قذف وفي الخلاصة الفتوى على هذا ا هـ . فقد اختلف الترجيح. وفي فتح القدير في شرح قوله ولا يقضى على غائب»: والذي يقتضيه النظر أن نفاذ القضاء على الغائب موقوف على تنفيذ قاض أخر لأن نفس القضاء مجتهد وسيأتي إيضاحه قريباً. وفي الإصلاح ويمضي حكم قاض. قال في الإيضاح : لم يقل حاكم احترازاً عن الحكم لأن الحكم فيه غير هذا ولم يقيده بقوله «آخر» ليعم حكم نفسه فيه ا اهـ. قبل ذلك اهـ . رضي وهي :
I.e., but the mujtahid's reasoning is that this evidence (whether it constitutes a proof for judgment without a present opponent) then if he judges by it, it is executed just as if he judged by the testimony of one who had been flogged for slander. And in al-Khulasa, the fatwa is on this. So there is disagreement on the preferred view. And in Fath al-Qadir, in explaining his statement 'and he does not judge against an absent party': 'What the sound view requires is that the enforcement of a judgment against an absent party is dependent on execution by another judge, because the judgment itself is a matter of ijtihad, and its clarification will come soon.' And in al-Islah: 'And the judgment of a judge is executed.' He said in al-Idah: 'He did not say "ruler" to avoid confusion with the ruling, because the ruling here is different, and he did not restrict it with "another" to include his own judgment in that.' End. Before that, etc. Radi wa hiya:
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage addresses the important procedural issue of judgments rendered without the presence of the defendant. The commentator [Ibn Nujaym] explains that according to some, a judgment based solely on evidence presented by the plaintiff without the defendant being present is valid and enforceable immediately, similar to other valid judgments. However, the more sound position, as stated in Fath al-Qadir, is that such a judgment is not immediately enforceable; rather, its execution is contingent upon another judge implementing it. This is because the permissibility of judging without the absent party is itself a matter of ijtihad. The commentator also notes the nuance that a judge's own judgment (حكم نفسه) is included in the scope of what may be executed, as long as it is not contradictory. The text then transitions to the next topic.

Key Terms
قضاء على غائب (qada' 'ala gha'ib): A legal judgment passed without the presence of the defendant
تنفيذ قاض أخر (tanfidh qadin akhar): Execution of the judgment by another judge

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fath al-Qadir as cited in the lesson, what condition is required for the enforcement of a judgment against an absent party?
A) Immediate enforcement by the same judge
B) Execution by another judge
C) The defendant's consent
D) A higher court's confirmation

Key Takeaway
A judgment against an absent party is valid, but its enforcement is conditional on execution by a different judge according to the preferred Hanafi position.

Inward Effect of Judgment on False Testimony: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on the inward effect of a judgment based on false testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi dispute on the inward enforceability of a judgment based on false testimony, identify the basis for each position, and explain the practical consequence.

Core Idea
A judgment based on false testimony is valid outwardly, but whether it binds inwardly depends on the type of case and whose view you follow.

In this passage, we learn about an important distinction in Hanafi qada: the effect of a judgment that was based on false testimony. Although the judgment is valid and enforceable, a disagreement arises between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding its binding effect in the sight of God. This has significant implications for the parties' moral obligations after the verdict.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling in the matn
The base text says the judgment is enforced outwardly and inwardly in contracts and dissolutions, but not in absolute ownerships. Note this is Abu Hanifa's position.
The matn is assuming Abu Hanifa's view.
2
Identify the disagreement of the two disciples
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is enforced only outwardly, not inwardly. They base this on the fact that false testimony is a valid proof only in the court, not in reality.
They compare it to a disqualified witness.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proofs
Abu Hanifa cites the saying of Ali to a woman: 'Your two witnesses have married you.' This indicates that the judgment is binding in reality. Also, the purpose of judgment is to cut off dispute completely.
The hadith is a qawl sahabi, considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze the rebuttal of the li'an analogy
The text mentions a counterargument from the case of li'an (mutual imprecation). The commentator says it is not convincing because the lie in li'an is about the accusation, not the separation itself.
This shows the careful examination of analogies.
5
Determine the practical consequence and fatwa hierarchy
The thamarah al-khilaf: if enforced inwardly, the husband may sleep with his wife even if he knows the testimony was false; if only outwardly, he must abstain. Later authorities differ on which view to follow: Abu al-Layth favors Sahibayn, while Fath al-Qadir in Nikah favors Abu Hanifa.
This shows that the mufta bihi is not uniform across all chapters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وينفذ القضاء بشهادة الزور في العقود والفسوخ ظاهراً وباطناً لا في الأملاك المرسلة) أي المطلقة التي لم يذكر لها سبب معين وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : لا ينفذ إلا ظاهراً لأن شهادة الزور حجة ظاهراً فصار كما لو كان غير أهل لها، وله قول علي الله عنه لتلك المرأة شاهداك زوجاك ولأن القضاء لقطع المنازعة بينهما من كل وجه فلو لم ينفذ باطناً كان تمهيداً لها. وفي فتح القدير : وأما الاستشهاد بتفريق المتلاعنين فليس بشيء ا هـ. يعني باعتبار أن الكذب ليس هو في الأخبار بالفرقة وإنما هو في الرمي بالزنا أو نفي الولد. وقال الفقيه أبو الليث الفتوى على قولهما. وفي فتح القدير من النكاح: وقول أبي حنيفة هو الوجه.
His statement: 'And the judgment is enforced with false testimony in contracts and dissolutions, outwardly and inwardly, not in absolute ownerships' i.e., those unrestricted that have no specific cause. And this is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two said: It is not enforced except outwardly, because false testimony is a proof outwardly, so it becomes as if they were not qualified for it. And he has the saying of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, to that woman: 'Your two witnesses have married you.' And because judgment is to cut off dispute between them completely, so if it were not enforced inwardly, it would be a preparation for it. And in Fath al-Qadir: 'As for citing the separation of spouses in li'an, it is not convincing.' meaning considering that the lie is not in reporting the separation but in the accusation of adultery or denial of paternity. And al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: The fatwa is on their statement (the two disciples). And in Fath al-Qadir from the Book of Nikah: 'And Abu Hanifa's view is the correct one.'
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage addresses the important question of the effect of a judicial decision based on false testimony. The matn states that such a judgment is enforced both outwardly (in the worldly court) and inwardly (in the sight of God) in matters of contracts (such as sale, marriage) and dissolutions (such as divorce, rescission), but not in absolute ownerships (الأملاك المرسلة) – those without a specified cause, like claiming ownership of property without a transaction. Abu Hanifa holds that the judgment is effective both outwardly and inwardly because the purpose of judgment is to settle disputes completely. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that it is only effective outwardly because false testimony is a valid proof only in the worldly sense; inwardly, the truth prevails. They compare it to a witness who is disqualified (like a slave or non-Muslim). Abu Hanifa supports his view with the hadith of Ali who said to a woman concerning a disputed marriage: 'Your two witnesses have married you.' This indicates that the judgment is binding in reality. The commentator then notes that the fatwa according to Abu al-Layth is on the view of the two disciples, but in Fath al-Qadir from the Nikah section, Abu Hanifa's view is considered stronger. Later, the author will elaborate on branches and conditions.

Key Terms
شهادة الزور (shahadat al-zur): Testimony that is known to be false by the witnesses themselves, but outwardly appears valid.
ظاهراً وباطناً (zahiran wa batinan): Outwardly (in the worldly legal system) and inwardly (in the sight of God, i.e., the actual truth).
الأملاك المرسلة (al-amlak al-mursala): Absolute ownerships, i.e., claims of ownership without a specific cause or transaction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Abu Hanifa's view that a judgment based on false testimony is effective both outwardly and inwardly in contracts and dissolutions?
A) A hadith of the Prophet
B) The saying of Ali 'Your two witnesses have married you'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Rational analogy with valid testimony

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that a judge's ruling based on false testimony is valid outwardly, but its inward effect depends on the nature of the case and which opinion is followed.
