Two Conditions for Inward Enforcement of Judgment on False Testimony
Branches and conditions for inward enforcement of judgment on false testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for the inward enforcement of a judgment based on false testimony and apply them to cases involving marriage, divorce, and sale.

Core Idea
A judgment based on false testimony is only inwardly enforceable if the judge is ignorant of the falsehood and the subject matter is capable of creation.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we examine the practical branches and the two conditions that determine whether a judgment based on false testimony is enforceable both outwardly and inwardly. While the outward effect of a judge's ruling is always binding, the inward effect depends on the judge's knowledge and the nature of the case. Understanding these conditions is crucial for distinguishing between apparent validity and actual truth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
From the text, extract the two conditions for inward enforcement: the judge must be unaware of the falsehood, and the subject must be capable of creation.
These are stated explicitly in al-Walwaljiyya.
2
Apply the first condition
Consider the branches where the judge's ignorance matters. For example, if the judge knows the witnesses are lying, the judgment is not inwardly enforced.
This is emphasized in Fath al-Qadir.
3
Apply the second condition
Check if the subject matter can be created by the judgment. For instance, a marriage with a woman already under a husband cannot be created, so the judgment is not inwardly enforced.
Examples include a woman in iddah, apostate, or prohibited by fosterage.
4
Note intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Muhammad agreed with Abu Hanifa in the branch about captive children because he does not know the reality of the falsehood. This shows a specific application of the first condition.
Refer to Fath al-Qadir for this detail.
5
Distinguish from false oaths and disqualified witnesses
Judgments based on false oaths are not inwardly enforced, and testimony from slaves, non-Muslims, or those flogged for slander is not enforced at all, even outwardly.
The passage explicitly excludes these cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن فروع المسألة: ادعى على امرأة نكاحاً وهي جاحدة وأقام بينة زور فقضى بالنكاح بينهما حل للمدعي وطؤها ولها التمكين عنده، وكذا إذا ادعت نكاحاً على رجل وهو يجحد ومنها قضى ببيع أمة بشهادة زور حل للمنكر وطؤها، وكذا في الفسوخ بالبيع والإقالة ومنها ادعت أنه طلقها ثلاثاً وهو ينكر وأقامت بينة زور فقضى بالفرقة فتزوجت بآخر بعد العدة حل له وطؤها عند الله تعالى وإن علم بحقيقة الحال وحل لأحد الشاهدين أن يتزوجها ويطأها ولا يحل للأول وطؤها ولا يحل لها تمكينه. ومن صور وصبية سبيا فكبرا وأعتقا ثم تزوج أحدهما بالآخر فجاء حربي مسلماً وأقام التحريم: صبي بينة أنهما ولداه قضى القاضي بينهما بالفرقة، فإن رجع الشهود أو تبين أنهم شهود زور لا يحل للزوج وطؤها عنده لأن القضاء بالحرمة نفذ باطناً وظاهراً، ومحمد في هذا الفرع مع أبي حنيفة لأنه لا يعلم حقيقة كذب الشهود. كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الولوالجية: وأثم الشاهدان إثماً عظيماً وللنفاذ باطناً عنده شرطان: الأول عدم علم القاضي بكذبهم فلو علم القاضي كذب الشهود لم ينفذ؛ ذكره في فتح القدير من النكاح الثاني كون المحل قابلاً فإذا كانت المرأة تحت زوج أو كانت معتدة أو مرتدة أو محرمة بمصاهرة أو برضاع لم ينفذ لأنه لا يقبل الإنشاء، وإنما لا يشترط حضور الشهود للنكاح على قول بعض المشايخ . وفي شرح الجامع لقاضيخان : ولم يشترط محمد حضور الشهود وذكر الزعفراني أنه شرط وبه أخذ عامة المشايخ ا هـ . فالمعتمد الاشتراط وإذا قلنا بعدمه وهو أوجه كما في فتح القدير من النكاح فوجهه أنا نجعل حكم الحاكم إنشاء مقتض في ضمن صحة القضاء والثابت اقتضاء لا تراعى فيه شرائطه، وكذا لا يشترط قبض رأس المال وبدل الصرف قبل الافتراق كما في القنية . قيد بشهادة الزور لأن القاضي لو قضى بشهادتهم فظهر أنهم عبيد أو كفار أو محدودون في قذف لم ينفذ إجماعاً لأنها ليست بحجة أصلاً بخلاف الفساق على ما عرف، ولإمكان الوقوف عليهم فلم تكن شهادتهم حجة وقيد بالشهادة لأن القضاء باليمين الكاذبة لا ينفذ قالوا : لو ادعت أن زوجها أبانها بثلاث فأنكر فحلفه القاضي فحلف والمرأة تعلم أن الأمر كما قالت لا يسعها الإقامة معه ولا أن تأخذ من ميراثه شيئاً، وهذا لا يشكل إذا كان ثلاثاً لبطلان المحلية للإنشاء قبل زوج آخر وفيما دون الثلاث مشكل لأنه يقبل الإنشاء وأجيب بأنه يثبت إذا قضى القاضي بالنكاح وهنا لم يقض به لاعترافهما به وإنما ادعت الفرقة ؛ كذا ذكر الشارح. وفي الخلاصة : ولا يحل وطؤها إجماعاً. وفي البزازية قبيل الإيمان : سمعت بطلاق زوجها إياها ثلاثاً ولا تقدر على منعه إلا بقتله إن علمت أنه يقربها تقتله بالدواء ولا تقتل نفسها. وذكر الأوزجندي أنها ترفع الأمر إلى القاضي فإن لم يكن لها بينة تحلفه فإن حلف فالإثم عليه، وإن قتلته فلا شيء عليها والبائن كالثلاث ا هـ . وأطلق في العقود فشمل عقود التبرعات قالوا : وفي الهبة والصدقة روايتان وكذا في البيع بأقل من قيمته في رواية لا ينفذ باطناً لأن القاضي لا يملك إنشاء التبرعات في ملك الغير والبيع بالأقل تبرع من وجه وإطلاق الكتاب يقتضي أن المعتمد النفاذ فيها باطناً أيضاً لأن النفاذ في ضمن صحة القضاء فلا يشترط فيه شرائطه ولا يختص بمحل والبيع بالأقل يملكه من لا يملك التبرع كالمكاتب والعبد المأذون . وفي إيضاح الإصلاح : أراد بالفسخ إبطال العقود بأي وجه كان فيعم الطلاق ا هـ. لأن الطلاق لا يبطل النكاح وإنما يرفع القيد الثابت بالنكاح فالأولى أن يقال أراد بالفسخ ما يرفع حكم العقد فيشمل الطلاق كما لا يخفى. وفي القنية : ادعى عليه جارية أنه اشتراها بكذا فأنكر فحلف فنكل فقضى عليه بالنكول تحل الجارية للمدعي ديانة وقضاء في شهادة الزور ا هـ . فعلى هذا القضاء بالنكول كالقضاء بشهادة الزور، وظاهر اقتصاره على نفي الأملاك المرسلة أنه لا ينفذ باطناً في النسب وقدمنا أنه ينفذ فيه وصرح به الولوالجي وليس بصحيح كما
From the branches of the issue: If someone claims marriage to a woman and she denies, and he presents false witnesses, and the judge rules for marriage, it is lawful for the claimant to have intercourse with her and she must submit to him. Similarly if the woman claims marriage. Likewise, if the judge rules a sale of a slave-girl based on false testimony, the buyer may have intercourse with her. Similarly in dissolutions by sale and rescission. Also, if a woman claims her husband divorced her three times while he denies, and she presents false witnesses, and the judge rules separation, then she marries another after the waiting period, it is lawful for the second husband to have intercourse with her even if she knows the truth. But it is not lawful for the first husband to have intercourse with her, nor for her to allow him. And from the examples: a boy and a girl who were captured in war, grew up, were freed, then married each other, then a Muslim captive came and presented evidence that they are his children, and the judge ruled separation between them. If the witnesses recant or are found to be false, the husband cannot have intercourse with her because the judgment of prohibition is enforced both inwardly and outwardly. And Muhammad is with Abu Hanifa in this branch because he does not know the reality of the witnesses' falsehood. In al-Walwaljiyya: The two witnesses commit a great sin. For inward enforcement there are two conditions: first, the judge's ignorance of their falsehood; if he knows they are lying, it is not enforced. Second, the subject must be capable of creation; if the woman is under a husband, or in waiting period, or apostate, or prohibited by fosterage, etc., it is not enforced because it cannot be created. The presence of witnesses for marriage is not required according to some, but the relied-upon position is that it is required. It is also not required to have possession of the capital or the exchange in a currency exchange before separation. The restriction to false testimony is because if the judge rules based on the testimony of slaves, non-Muslims, or those flogged for slander, it is not enforced by consensus. Also, a judgment based on a false oath is not enforced. Example: a woman claims her husband divorced her three times, he swears, she knows he is lying. She cannot live with him or inherit from him. If the divorce is triple, it is clear; if less, there is an issue. Also, in cases of oaths and killing for protection, etc. The generality of contracts includes gratuitous contracts, but there are two narrations about gifts and charity and selling at a low price. The correct view is that they are enforced inwardly because enforcement is within the validity of the judgment. The judgment based on refusal to take an oath (nukul) is like that based on false testimony. It appears that the restriction to absolute ownerships implies that it is not enforced inwardly in lineage, but we already mentioned it is enforced in lineage.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage provides numerous practical examples illustrating the application of the rule regarding judgments based on false testimony. The key points: In marriage claims, if the judge rules in favor based on false testimony, the marriage is valid both outwardly and inwardly, so the claimant can have intercourse with the woman even if she knows the truth. Similarly in divorce cases, if a woman falsely claims triple divorce and gets a ruling, she can marry another. However, if the judge knows the witnesses are false, or if the subject matter cannot be created (like a marriage that already exists or a woman in iddah), the judgment is not inwardly effective. The passage also discusses conditions: the judge's ignorance and the capacity for creation. Additionally, it distinguishes false testimony from false oaths and from testimony of disqualified witnesses. The various branches show the depth of Hanafi jurisprudence in applying general principles to specific cases, emphasizing that the outward effect of a judge's ruling is binding, but the inward effect depends on the actual truth and the conditions mentioned.

Key Terms
شرطان للنفاذ باطناً (shartan li al-nafadh batinan): Two conditions for the inward enforcement of a judgment based on false testimony: judge's ignorance and subject's capacity.
النكول (al-nukul): Refusal to take an oath when required; judgment based on nukul is analogous to judgment based on false testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for a judgment based on false testimony to be enforced inwardly?
A) The judge must be aware that the witnesses are truthful.
B) The subject matter must be capable of being created.
C) The witnesses must be Muslim and male.
D) The judgment must be unanimous.

Key Takeaway
The inward enforcement of a judgment based on false testimony is conditional upon the judge's ignorance and the capacity of the subject matter.

The Qawida: Qada Overrides Ra'y but Not Vice Versa
Maxim with four sub-rules and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sub-rules of the qawida regarding qada and ra'y and apply them to simple scenarios.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling ends debate—it overrides personal opinion, but opinion cannot undo a final judgment.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq draws on al-Nutaf to present a foundational maxim in Islamic judicial theory. It clarifies the binding force of qada (judicial ruling) versus the non-binding nature of ra'y (personal ijtihad). Understanding this maxim is essential for any student of Hanafi fiqh, as it governs the finality of court decisions and the limits of personal legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sub-rules
Read the maxim carefully and list the four distinct pairwise interactions between qada and ra'y as stated: (1) qada does not demolish qada, (2) ra'y does not demolish ra'y, (3) qada demolishes ra'y, (4) ra'y does not demolish qada.
Each sub-rule is a complete prohibition or affirmation.
2
Understand each sub-rule's meaning
For each sub-rule, ask: what specific action is being prohibited or allowed? For example, 'qada does not demolish qada' means a judge cannot overturn a prior valid ruling by another judge.
The sub-rules are not symmetrical; their logical relationships are key.
3
Work through the provided examples
The text gives examples: the second sub-rule (ra'y does not demolish ra'y) uses the case of a husband changing his opinion on the number of divorces; the third sub-rule (qada demolishes ra'y) uses a judge ruling the divorce revocable; the fourth sub-rule (ra'y does not demolish qada) uses a judge's change of opinion.
Map each example to its corresponding sub-rule.
4
Recognize practical implications
Consider how this maxim ensures stability: once a judge issues a binding ruling, it cannot be undone by personal opinion or even by the judge's own later change of mind.
This principle is foundational for the authority of Islamic courts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي آخر النتف : اعلم أن القضاء لا يهدم والرأي لا يهدم الرأي والقضاء يهدم الرأي والرأي لا يهدم القضاء مثلا الأوّل ظاهر، وأما مثال الثاني فإن يعتقد الثلاث في قوله أنت طالق ألبتة فإنها تحرم عليه فإن تحول رأيه إلى أنها رجعية لم تحل. ومثال الثالث أن يحكم القاضي بكونها رجعية فإن هذا القضاء يهدم رأيه من أنها ثلاث. ومثال الرابع إذا قضى قاض ثم تحول رأيه فإنه لا ينقض ما مضى لأن الرأي لا القضاء وإنما يعمل برأيه في المستقبل ا هـ مختصراً .
And in the end of [Kitab] al-Nutaf: Know that qada (judicial ruling) does not demolish [another qada], and ra'y (personal opinion) does not demolish ra'y, and qada demolishes ra'y, but ra'y does not demolish qada. The first example is clear. As for the second example: if he believes [the divorce is] three in his saying 'You are irrevocably divorced', then she becomes forbidden to him; if his opinion changes to thinking it is revocable, she does not become permissible. The third example: if the judge rules it to be revocable, then this qada demolishes his opinion that it was three. The fourth example: if a judge passes a ruling, then his opinion changes, he does not nullify what has passed, because [it is] ra'y, not qada; he only acts according to his opinion in the future. End summary.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq quotes al-Nutaf to present a foundational qawida (maxim) in qada: four rules about the interaction of judicial rulings and personal ijtihad. (1) Qada does not nullify another qada – thus a judge cannot overturn a prior judge's ruling. (2) Ra'y does not nullify ra'y – a person's own change of ijtihad does not retroactively change the ruling that was based on his earlier opinion. (3) Qada nullifies ra'y – a judge's ruling binds even if it contradicts the person's ijtihad. Example: If a husband believes his divorce is final, but a judge rules it revocable, the judge's ruling prevails and he may stay with her. (4) Ra'y does not nullify qada – if a judge later changes his own ijtihad, he cannot retroactively undo his past judgments, only act on his new opinion going forward.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada): A judge's final ruling issued with binding authority to settle a dispute.
الرأي (al-ra'y): Personal ijtihad or opinion of a scholar or layperson, lacking binding force.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida, if a judge's ruling conflicts with a person's personal ijtihad, which prevails?
A) The personal ijtihad (ra'y) prevails
B) The judge's ruling (qada) prevails
C) Neither; a new judge must decide
D) It depends on the school of the person

Key Takeaway
Qada overrides ra'y, but ra'y cannot undo qada—this ensures finality of judicial rulings and respect for authority.

Ruling on Judging an Absent Party (al-Qada' ala al-Gha'ib)
Ruling with proof and intra-madhhab difference on enforcement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on judging an absent party without a representative, explain the hadith proof, and describe the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on enforceability (nufudh).

Core Idea
Judgment against an absent party is invalid without a representative; its enforceability is disputed to protect the madhhab.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling in Kanz al-Daqa'iq that a judge may not pass judgment on an absent litigant unless a representative (wakeel or wasi) is present. It provides the hadith proof and then delves into the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether such a ruling, if issued, can be enforced. The relied-upon position is non-enforcement to safeguard the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is a judge passing judgment against an absent party (gha'ib) who has no representative. The ruling: it is invalid (la yasihh).
The matn says 'nor is judgment passed against an absent' and commentary interprets that as invalidity.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author cites the hadith: 'Do not judge between two litigants until you hear the statement of the other.' This is a sound hadith reported by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and Tirmidhi.
The hadith is the core dalil; its transmission is zanni (ahad) but its meaning is clear.
3
Understand the rationale
Judgment cuts off dispute (qat' al-munaza'ah). Here there is no dispute because the absent party has not denied anything (no inkār). Hence, judgment is not valid. The presence of the opponent is a condition to verify denial.
This is a logical (talil) argument based on the purpose of qada.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on nufudh
Even if a judge issues a ruling against an absent party, its enforceability (nufudh) is disputed. Two narrations: one says it is enforceable if another judge who holds it valid enforces it; the other says it is never enforceable. Many later scholars, including Imam Dhaheer al-Din, give fatwa on non-enforcement.
The dispute is about the effect after the ruling is made, not its initial validity.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is non-enforcement (la yanfudh). This is chosen to prevent undermining the Hanafi school (kayla yataṭarraqū ilā ibṭāl madhhab aṣḥābinā).
Al-Ramli clarifies that the ikhtilaf is about the permissibility of the judge's action, not about nufudh itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأملاك المرسلة ولا يقضى على غائب إلا أن يحضر من يقوم مقامه كالوكيل والوصي قوله : (ولا يقضى على غائب) أي لا يصح القضاء على غير خصم حاضر لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لعلي لا تقض لأحد الخصمين حتى تسمع كلام الآخر فإنك إذا سمعت كلام الآخر علمت كيف تقضي » (۱) رواه أحمد وأبو داود والترمذي. ولأن القضاء لقطع المنازعة ولا منازعة هنا لعدم الإنكار فلا يصح ؛ كذا ذكره الشارح. وصرح في فتح القدير بأن حضرة الخصم ليتحقق إنكاره شرط لصحة الحكم. وفي البزازية من القضاء: قضى للغائب أو عليه لا يصح إلا أن يكون عنه خصم حاضر ا هـ . فلذا فسرنا كلام الصحة لا بعدم الحل والأولى أن يفسر بعدم النفاذ لقولهم إذا نفذه قاض آخر يراه فإنه ينفذ، وقدمنا خلاف التصحيح في نفاذ القضاء على الغائب فصحح الشارح عدمه، وفي الخلاصة والبزازية الفتوى على النفاذ الأول . في فتح القدير وأنه لا بد من إمضاء قاض آخر لأن ورجح الاختلاف في نفس القضاء. وفي البزازية من القضاء قال الإمام ظهير الدين: في نفاذ القضاء على الغائب روايتان ونحن نفتي بعدم النفاذ كيلا يتطرقوا إلى إبطال مذهب أصحابنا اهـ. والقائب بأن الفتوى على النفاذ خواهر زاده وفي منية المفتي: القضاء على الغائب بلا خصم فيه روايتان ويفتى بعدم النفاذ، وقيل إن رآه قاض فقضى به ينفذ ا هـ . لكن اشتبه على كثير أن قولهم الفتوى على النفاذ أعم من كون القاضي شافعياً يراه أو حنفياً لا يراه وهو إنما هو فيمن يراه والظاهر أنه في حق من يراه لإجماع الحنفية على أنه لا يقضى على غائب كما ذكره قوله: (فلذا فسرنا كلام المصنف بعدم الصحة قال الرملي هذا لا يتأتى على القول بأن الخلاف في حل الأقدام لا في حل النفاذ فتنبه قوله : (كيلا يتطرقوا إلى إبطال مذهب أصحابنا) قال الرملي : فإن قلت ما وجه التطرق إلى إبطال المذهب في هذه المسألة دون غيرها . الخلافيات؟ قلت : من لم أر من ذكر وجهه ويمكن أن يقال : لأن القضاء لا يخلو إما على حاضر أو على غائب، فإذا فتح باب القضاء على الغائب فقد ترك منه النصف بخلاف غيرها من المسائل الخلافية والله تعالى أعلم لا قوله : (والظاهر أنه في حق من يراه الخ) لم يذكر ما لو كان ممن يراه الحنفي، ولا شك أنه يجري فيه الكلام المار فيما لو قضى في المجتهد فيه مخالف لرأيه من كونه ناسياً أو عامداً وما فيه من الخلاف بين الإمام وصاحبيه واختلاف الترجيح وأن هذا في غير قضاة زماننا قال الرملي في جامع الفصولين
Unrestricted properties, and judgment cannot be passed against an absent party unless someone representing him is present, like a wakeel or wasi. His statement: (Nor is judgment passed against an absent) i.e., judgment upon a non-present opponent is not valid, due to his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'Do not judge between two litigants until you hear the statement of the other, for when you hear the statement of the other, you will know how to judge.' (Ahmad, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). And because judgment is to cut off dispute, and here there is no dispute due to lack of denial, so it is not valid. Thus the commentator mentioned. And it is stated in Fath al-Qadir that the presence of the opponent to verify his denial is a condition for the validity of the ruling. And in al-Bazzaziyyah on qada: Judgment for or against an absent party is not valid unless there is a present opponent on his behalf. Therefore we interpreted the statement [of the author] as invalidity, not non-permissibility; and it is better to interpret it as non-enforceability (nufudh), because of their statement: if another judge who holds it valid enforces it, it takes effect. And we previously presented the disagreement regarding correction on enforcement of judgment against an absent party; the corrector (sharih) upheld its non-enforcement. In al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyyah, the fatwa is on enforcement initially. In Fath al-Qadir: it is necessary for another judge to sign it, and he preferred the difference in the judgment itself. And in al-Bazzaziyyah from qada: Imam Dhaheer al-Din said: There are two narrations on enforcement of judgment against an absent party; we give fatwa on non-enforcement to prevent them from undermining the madhhab of our companions. Someone said that the fatwa is on enforcement (Khawahar Zadeh). In Munyat al-Mufti: Judgment against an absent without a representative has two narrations; fatwa is given on non-enforcement; it is said if a judge who holds it valid passes it, it enforces. But many are confused that their saying 'the fatwa is on enforcement' is general whether the judge is a Shafi'i who holds it valid or a Hanafi who does not; it is only for those who hold it valid. The apparent is that it is concerning those who hold it valid because of the consensus of Hanafis that judgment against an absent is not passed. As he said: (Therefore we interpreted the author's statement as invalidity). Al-Ramli said: This is not consistent with the view that the disagreement is on the permissibility of [the judge's] action, not on enforcement, so pay attention. His statement: (Lest they tread towards invalidating the madhhab of our companions). Al-Ramli said: If you say what is the face of treading to invalidate the madhhab in this issue unlike other disputed issues? I say: I have not seen anyone mention its face; and it can be said: Because judgment is either upon a present or an absent; if the door of judgment upon an absent is opened, then half of it has been left, unlike other disputed issues. And Allah knows best. His statement: (And the apparent is that it is concerning those who hold it valid) He did not mention the case if the judge is one who holds the Hanafi view. No doubt that the previous discussion applies: if he judges in a matter of ijtihad contrary to his own view, whether he is forgetful or deliberate, and the difference between the Imam and his two companions, and the variation in tarjih, and that this is not for the judges of our time. Al-Ramli said in Jami' al-Fusulayn.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling in Kanz al-Daqa'iq that a judge cannot pass judgment on an absent party (gha'ib) unless a representative (wakeel, wasi) is present. The commentator provides the hadith proof: the Prophet instructed Ali to hear both sides. The rationale is that judgment aims to end dispute, but there is no dispute without denial from the absent party. Then the passage discusses the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on nufudh (enforcement) of such a ruling even if it was issued incorrectly. The relied-upon view (fatwa) is that such a ruling does not take effect (la yanfudh) unless another judge who holds it valid enforces it. Imam Dhaheer al-Din explicitly says they give fatwa on non-enforcement to protect the madhhab from being undermined. The passage ends with a note from al-Ramli clarifying that the ikhtilaf is about the action of the judge (hal al-aqdām) in the first place, not about enforcement.

Key Terms
القضاء على الغائب (al-qada' 'ala al-gha'ib): A judge's ruling in favor of or against an absent litigant who has no representative present.
النفاذ (al-nufudh): Enforceability or legal effect of a court ruling.
الخصم (al-khasm): Litigant or opponent in a legal case.

The Ruling on Judgment in Absentia: Validity and Execution
A ruling with proof on the invalidity of judging absentees, with commentary on execution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on judgment in absentia, cite the hadith proof, and distinguish between validity (sihha) and enforceability (nufudh).

Core Idea
Judgment on an absentee is invalid without a present opponent; even if issued, its enforceability is contested among Hanafi scholars.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq: a judge may not pass a valid judgment on an absentee (gha'ib) unless a representative is present. The proof is drawn from the Prophet's instruction to Ali (ra). However, the commentary expands the discussion to distinguish between the validity of the judgment and its execution. We will explore the primary evidence, the intra-Hanafi disagreement on enforceability, and the correct interpretation of the matn's phrase 'لا يصح.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
What does the matn say? It states 'ولا يقضى على غائب' meaning judgment on an absentee is not valid. Identify that this concerns the validity of the judgment, not just permissibility.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The hadith of the Prophet to Ali: 'لا تقض لأحد الخصمين حتى تسمع كلام الآخر'. Understand how this hadith proves the ruling – the prohibition implies invalidity.
Narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi.
3
Analyze the 'illah (rationale)
Judgment is for cutting off dispute; without a present opponent, there is no denial (inkar) to create a dispute, so the judgment is invalid.
The rationale is explicitly given in the text.
4
Distinguish validity vs. enforceability
The matn's 'لا يصح' refers to validity. However, the commentator suggests it is better interpreted as non-execution (adam al-nufudh) because a subsequent judge can enforce it.
This distinction is the key expansion in the commentary.
5
Follow the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on enforcement
Some authorities (al-Khulasah, al-Bazzaziyyah) hold that such a judgment can be enforced if another judge confirms it; the commentator prefers non-enforcement.
Fath al-Qadir requires the approval of another judge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يقضى على غائب) أي لا يصح القضاء على غير خصم حاضر لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لعلي لا تقض لأحد الخصمين حتى تسمع كلام الآخر فإنك إذا سمعت كلام الآخر علمت كيف تقضي رواه أحمد وأبو داود والترمذي. ولأن القضاء لقطع المنازعة ولا منازعة هنا لعدم الإنكار فلا يصح ؛ كذا ذكره الشارح. وصرح في فتح القدير بأن حضرة الخصم ليتحقق إنكاره شرط لصحة الحكم. وفي البزازية من القضاء: قضى للغائب أو عليه لا يصح إلا أن يكون عنه خصم حاضر ا هـ . فلذا فسرنا كلام الصحة لا بعدم الحل والأولى أن يفسر بعدم النفاذ لقولهم إذا نفذه قاض آخر يراه فإنه ينفذ، وقدمنا خلاف التصحيح في نفاذ القضاء على الغائب فصحح الشارح عدمه، وفي الخلاصة والبزازية الفتوى على النفاذ الأول . في فتح القدير وأنه لا بد من إمضاء قاض آخر لأن ورجح الاختلاف في نفس القضاء.
His saying: (And he does not judge on an absentee) meaning: judgment is not valid on a non-present opponent, due to his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'Do not judge for one of the two litigants until you hear the statement of the other, for if you hear the statement of the other you will know how to judge.' Narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi. And because judgment is for cutting off dispute, and there is no dispute here due to the lack of denial, so it is not valid; thus mentioned by the commentator. And it is explicitly stated in Fath al-Qadir that the presence of the opponent to verify his denial is a condition for the validity of the judgment. And in al-Bazzaziyyah from the section on judgment: He judged for an absentee or against him, it is not valid unless there is a present opponent on his behalf. So for that reason we interpreted his words as referring to validity, not permissibility. And it is better to interpret it as non-execution because they said: If another judge who holds that view executes it, it is executed. And we have already presented the differing correction regarding the execution of judgment on an absentee; the commentator corrected its non-existence, and in al-Khulasah and al-Bazzaziyyah the fatwa is on execution. In Fath al-Qadir, it is stated that there must be the approval of another judge because the disagreement is in the judgment itself.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof: a judge cannot pass a valid judgment on an absentee (gha'ib) without a present opponent (khasm hadir). The proof is the hadith where the Prophet ﷺ instructed Ali not to judge until hearing both sides. The reasoning is that judgment aims to resolve disputes, and without denial or claim, there is no dispute. The commentator notes that the condition of the opponent's presence is for validity (sihhah). However, there is a difference of opinion on whether such a judgment, if issued, is enforceable (nafidh). Some say it is not executable unless another judge who holds it valid confirms it. The passage clarifies that when the text says 'لا يصح' (not valid), it refers to validity in the sense of not being legally sound, not that it is prohibited (haram). The better interpretation is that it is non-executable, but if another judge executes it, it becomes effective.

Key Terms
الغائب (al-ghā'ib): The person against whom a claim is made but who is not present at the court session.
النفاذ (al-nufūdh): The execution or enforceability of a judgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A judge cannot pass a valid judgment on an absentee without a present opponent; proof is the hadith and the rationale of dispute resolution; enforceability remains a debated point within the Hanafi school.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Execution of Absentee Judgment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on execution of absentee judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations on executing absentee judgments, explain the reasoning for non-execution, and apply al-Ramli's flexible approach to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Judgment on an absentee: two narrations, but executing it risks undermining the Hanafi madhhab.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: can a judge execute a judgment against an absentee without a present opponent? The source reveals conflicting transmissions from the founding imams and later scholars. We will trace the arguments for and against execution, understand why some scholars fear opening this door, and see how later authorities like al-Ramli recommend a case-by-case evaluation balancing caution and necessity. By the end, you will grasp not only the ruling but the method of scholarly ijtihad within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
The passage concerns whether a judgment against an absentee (without a present opponent) is enforceable (nafidh). Note that the Hanafi school generally does not permit such judgments, but there is an internal difference.
The issue is about execution (nufudh), not the validity of the judgment itself.
2
Trace the two narrations (riwayatan)
From the imams, there are two narrations: one allowing execution, one not. Scholars like Zahir al-Din choose non-execution to protect the madhhab, while others like Kharzadah prefer execution.
The two narrations reflect a genuine ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Analyze the argument for non-execution
Zahir al-Din argues that if absentee judgments are routinely executed, opponents might use it to weaken the Hanafi position. Al-Ramli clarifies the dispute is about whether to initiate such a case, not about execution after it is done.
The reasoning is strategic: preserving the school's coherence.
4
Critique the claim of consensus
Al-Bazzazi claimed consensus on execution, but the author rejects this, noting it contradicts the two narrations. The passage calls it an 'astonishing' claim and a false consensus.
This shows how later scholars scrutinize transmission reliability.
5
Apply the flexible approach
Mahmud in Jami' al-Fusulayn recommends that judges and muftis consider the specific circumstances, hardship, and necessity, giving fatwa accordingly. This is a practical solution for modern cases.
The school does not rigidly adhere to one view; it allows contextual ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقدمنا خلاف التصحيح في نفاذ القضاء على الغائب فصحح الشارح عدمه، وفي الخلاصة والبزازية الفتوى على النفاذ الأول . في فتح القدير وأنه لا بد من إمضاء قاض آخر لأن ورجح الاختلاف في نفس القضاء. وفي البزازية الغائب بلا خصم فيه روايتان ويفتى بعدم النفاذ، وقيل إن رآه قاض فقضى به ينفذ ا هـ . لكن اشتبه على كثير أن قولهم الفتوى على النفاذ أعم من كون القاضي شافعياً يراه أو حنفياً لا يراه وهو إنما هو فيمن يراه والظاهر أنه في حق من يراه لإجماع الحنفية على أنه لا يقضى على غائب كما ذكره قوله: (فلذا فسرنا كلام المصنف بعدم الصحة قال الرملي هذا لا يتأتى على القول بأن الخلاف في حل الأقدام لا في حل النفاذ فتنبه قوله : (كيلا يتطرقوا إلى إبطال مذهب أصحابنا) قال الرملي : فإن قلت ما وجه التطرق إلى إبطال المذهب في هذه المسألة دون غيرها . الخلافيات؟ قلت : من لم أر من ذكر وجهه ويمكن أن يقال : لأن القضاء لا يخلو إما على حاضر أو على غائب، فإذا فتح باب القضاء على الغائب فقد ترك منه النصف بخلاف غيرها من المسائل الخلافية والله تعالى أعلم لا قوله : (والظاهر أنه في حق من يراه الخ) لم يذكر ما لو كان ممن يراه الحنفي، ولا شك أنه يجري فيه الكلام المار فيما لو قضى في المجتهد فيه مخالف لرأيه من كونه ناسياً أو عامداً وما فيه من الخلاف بين الإمام وصاحبيه واختلاف الترجيح وأن هذا في غير قضاة زماننا قال الرملي في جامع الفصولين الصدر الشهيد في شرح أدب القضاء، ولو كان أعم للزم هدم مذهب أصحابنا، والعجب من البزازي حيث قال في الفتاوى من المفقود وهل ينصب القاضي وكيلا على الغائب وعن الغائب عندنا لا يفعل أما لو فعل بأن حكم على الغائب نفذ إجماعاً لأن المجتهد سبب أن البينة هل تكون حجة بلا خصم حاضر للقضاء أم لا ؛ فإذا رآها حجة وحكم نفذ وهو القضاء كما لو حكم بشهادة الفساق وعليه الفتوى ا هـ . فإن دعوى الإجماع ليست بصحيحة وهو مسبوق بها عن خواهرزاده وفي قوله فإذا رآها حجة إشارة إلى أنه ممن يرى القضاء على الغائب فخرج الحنفي المقلد ولقد صدق العلامة محمود حيث قال في جامع الفصولين : قد اضطرب آراؤهم وبيانهم في مسائل الحكم للغائب وعليه ولم يصف ولم ينقل عنهم أصل قوي ظاهر يبني عليه الفروع بلا اضطراب ولا إشكال فالظاهر عندي أن يتأمل في الوقائع ويحتاط ويلاحظ الحرج والضرورات فيفتى بحسبها جوازاً أو فساداً
And we have already presented the differing correction regarding the execution of judgment on an absentee; the commentator corrected its non-existence, and in al-Khulasah and al-Bazzaziyyah the fatwa is on execution. In Fath al-Qadir, it is stated that there must be the approval of another judge because the disagreement is in the judgment itself. And in al-Bazzaziyyah from the section on judgment, Imam Zahir al-Din said: Regarding the execution of judgment on an absentee, there are two narrations, and we give fatwa on non-execution so that they do not find a way to invalidate the madhhab of our companions. And al-Qa'ib said that the fatwa is on execution according to Kharzadah. And in Munyat al-Mufti: Judgment on an absentee without an opponent has two narrations, and fatwa is given on non-execution. It is said that if a judge sees it and passes judgment, it is executed. But many are confused that their statement 'the fatwa is on execution' is general, whether the judge is Shafi'i who holds it or Hanafi who does not, and it is only for those who hold it. The apparent meaning is that it is for those who hold it because of the consensus of the Hanafis that judgment is not passed on an absentee as he mentioned. His saying: (For that reason we interpreted the author's words as invalidity). Al-Ramli said: This does not follow on the view that the disagreement is about permissibility of initiating, not about execution, so pay attention. His saying: (So that they do not find a way to invalidate the madhhab of our companions). Al-Ramli said: If you ask what is the way to invalidate the madhhab in this issue as opposed to other issues of disagreement? I say: I have not seen anyone mention its reason, but it can be said: Because judgment is either on a present person or an absentee, so if the door of judgment on an absentee is opened, half of it is left, unlike other issues of disagreement. And Allah knows best. His saying: (And the apparent meaning is that it is for those who hold it, etc.) He did not mention what if the judge is one who holds it from the Hanafi school, and there is no doubt that the previous discussion applies regarding when a judge judges in a matter of ijtihad contrary to his own view, whether forgetful or deliberate, and the disagreement between the Imam and his two companions, and the difference in preponderance, and that this is not for the judges of our time. Al-Ramli said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: al-Sadr al-Shahid in Sharh Adab al-Qada'. And if it were general, it would necessitate the destruction of the madhhab of our companions. And it is astonishing from al-Bazzazi where he said in al-Fatawa from the section on the missing person: Is the judge appointed as a wakeel for the absentee and on behalf of the absentee? According to us, he does not do that. However, if he did by passing judgment on the absentee, it is executed by consensus because the mujtahid is the reason whether the evidence is proof without a present opponent for judgment or not; so if he considers it proof and judges, it is executed, just as if he judged by the testimony of sinners, and on that the fatwa is given. So the claim of consensus is not correct, and it is preceded by Kharzadah. And in his statement 'if he considers it proof' there is an indication that he is among those who see judging on an absentee, so it excludes the Hanafi muqallid. And indeed the scholar Mahmud spoke the truth when he said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: Their opinions and explanations have become confused in the issues of judgment for and against an absentee, and they did not describe nor transmit from them a strong apparent foundation upon which branches can be built without confusion or doubt. So the apparent view to me is that one should reflect on the incidents and exercise caution and consider hardship and necessities, and give fatwa accordingly, whether permissibility or invalidity.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage delves into the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a judgment passed on an absentee (without a present opponent) is enforceable (nafidh). The commentator mentions that there are two narrations (riwayatan) from the Hanafi imams: one allowing execution (nufudh) and one not. The fatwa in some works (al-Khulasah, al-Bazzaziyyah) is on execution, while Imam Zahir al-Din and others prefer non-execution to protect the madhhab from being undermined. Al-Ramli clarifies that the disagreement is about the permissibility of initiating such a judgment (hull al-aqdam), not about its execution once it has been passed. The passage also criticizes al-Bazzazi's claim of consensus on execution, stating it is not correct. The conclusion, quoting Mahmud in Jami' al-Fusulayn, acknowledges the confusion in the school and recommends that a judge or mufti should consider the specific circumstances, hardship (haraj), and necessity (darurah) when deciding, thus adopting a flexible approach rather than a rigid rule.

Key Terms
الرواية (al-riwāyah): A transmitted opinion from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on a legal issue.
النفاذ (al-nufūdh): The execution/enforceability of a judicial decision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Zahir al-Din, why is the fatwa given on non-execution of judgment on an absentee?
A) Because the hadith explicitly forbids it
B) To prevent people from using this to invalidate the Hanafi madhhab
C) Because the absentee might return and object
D) Because it is impossible to notify the absentee

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds two narrations on executing absentee judgments; the cautionary view of non-execution is preferred to protect the madhhab, but hardship permits flexibility.

Necessity and Caution in Absentee Judgments
Practical conclusion on absentee judgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that initiating judgment on an absentee is normally prohibited but becomes permissible when hardship and necessity require it to protect rights.

Core Idea
Absentee judgment is prohibited in Hanafi law, but necessity can make it permissible.

This passage concludes a lengthy discussion on judging absentees. The author reconciles the Hanafi default position (prohibition of initiation) with practical needs, showing that when hardship or necessity threatens rights, the permissive view may be followed. The key distinction is between initiating the case (prohibited) and executing the judgment (valid if issued by a permissive judge).

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
State the default Hanafi ruling on a judge initiating a case against an absentee without a representative. It is prohibited (haram).
This is the stronger position from the zahir al-riwayah.
2
Distinguish initiation vs execution
Understand that the prohibition concerns the judge's initiation of the case. If a judgment is passed (e.g., by a Shafi'i judge), its execution is valid without disagreement.
This resolves apparent contradictions in earlier texts.
3
Recognize intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that there are two narrations within the Hanafi school: one forbidding execution entirely, and one allowing it under necessity. The mufta bihi in hardship cases is permissibility.
Al-Ramli and Jami' al-Fusulayn favor the permissive view.
4
Apply conditions of hardship and necessity
The permissive ruling requires genuine hardship: inability to locate the absentee, bring him to court, or appoint a representative. The judge must be confident of the truth of the claim.
If the absentee can be reached, necessity is absent and the judgment is invalid.
5
Note the cautious alternative
The more cautious (ahwat) approach is to appoint a representative (wakil) for the absentee, which avoids the prohibition while protecting rights.
This is recommended when feasible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالظاهر عندي أن يتأمل في الوقائع ويحتاط ويلاحظ الحرج والضرورات فيفتى بحسبها جوازاً أو فساداً هـ. والذي ظهر لي من قنية مج : ليس للقاضي أن يقضي بالفرقة بسبب العجز عن النفقة وأجاب هو مراراً فيمن غاب عن امرأته وتركها بلا نفقة أنه لو قضى بالفرقة بسبب العجز عن النفقة ينقذ قال: وإنما فرقت بين الجوابين إذ الخلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى في حل الإقدام على القضاء فعنده يحل وعندنا لا يحل، ولا خلاف في النفاذ فالجواب الأوّل جواب عن الإقدام والثاني عن النفاذ مع حرمة الإقدام، ولا يشترط أن يكون شفعوي المذهب لأنه لا خلاف في نفاذ القضاء اهـ. فهو كما ترى صريح في أنه أعم وقوله فيما يأتي بعد أوراق ثلاث وفرقهم بين سبب وبين السبب والشرط أدل دليل على أن قولهم بنفاذ القضاء على الغائب في أظهر الروايتين إنما هو في قضاء الشافعي، وأما الحنفي فلا لأنه حينئذ لا معنى للفرق المذكور يرده ما تقدم من الخلاف في حل الإقدام فتأمل قوله : (فإن دعوى الإجماع ليست بصحيحة أي لما مر من أن الفتوى على عدم النفاذ لكن مر أيضاً أن الفتوى على النفاذ وعليه مشى البزازي فيما مر فكلامه هنا مبني عليه تأمل قوله: (فالظاهر عندي أن يتأمل الخ) تمام عبارته : مثلاً لو طلق امرأته عند العدل فغاب عن البلد ولا يعرف مكانه أو يعرف ولكن يعجز عن إحضاره أو عن أن تسافر إليه أو وكيلها لبعده أو لمانع آخر بأن كان لا يرضى أحد بالوكالة وكذا المديون لو غاب عن البلد وله نقد في البلد أو نحو ذلك ففي مثل هذه المواضع لو برهن على الغائب بحيث اطمأن قلب القاضي وغلب ظنه أنه حق لا تزوير ولا حيلة فيه فينبغي أن يحكم على الغائب وللغائب، وكذا للمفتي أن يفتي بجوازه دفعاً للحرج والضرورات وصيانة للحقوق عن الضياع مع أنه مجتهد فيه ذهب إلى جوازه الشافعي ومالك وأحمد بن حنبل، وفيه روايتان عن أصحابنا، والأحوط أن ينصب عن الغائب وكيل يعرف أنه يراعي جانب الغائب ولا يفرط في حقه فينصب الأولى ثم الأولى والله تعالى أعلم وأقره في نور العين إصلاح جامع الفصولين قوله : (ثم ظهر لي (الخ قال الرملي : لا يظهر التخصيص بالمفقود في كلامهم بل الظاهر التعميم، ثم إذا لوحظ الحرج والضرورة يجب اعتبار عدم مراجعة الغائب وإحضاره حتى لو أمكن لا يصح لعدم الضرورة
So the apparent view to me is that one should reflect on the incidents and exercise caution and consider hardship and necessities, and give fatwa accordingly, whether permissibility or invalidity. And what appeared to me from Qunyah is: The judge should not judge for separation due to inability to provide maintenance, and he answered repeatedly regarding someone who was absent from his wife and left her without maintenance, that if he judged for separation due to inability to provide maintenance, it is executed. He said: I differentiate between the two answers because the disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, is about the permissibility of initiating the judgment; according to him it is permissible, and according to us it is not. There is no disagreement about execution. So the first answer is about initiation, and the second is about execution along with the prohibition of initiation. It is not conditional that the judge be of the Shafi'i school because there is no disagreement about the execution of judgment. So it is, as you see, explicit that it is general. And his statement after three folios, 'and their differentiation between cause and condition' is the clearest evidence that their statement about execution of judgment on an absentee in the more apparent of the two narrations is only about the judgment of a Shafi'i judge. As for a Hanafi, not, because then there is no meaning for the mentioned difference. Refute it by what preceded about the disagreement in permissibility of initiation, so reflect. His saying: 'So the claim of consensus is not correct' means because of what passed that the fatwa is on non-execution, but it also passed that the fatwa is on execution, and al-Bazzazi followed that in what passed, so his statement here is based on that, so reflect. His saying: 'So the apparent view to me is to reflect, etc.' The complete expression: For example, if a man divorced his wife in the presence of a witness and then left the country and his whereabouts are unknown, or known but unable to bring him, or for her to travel to him, or her wakeel, due to distance or another obstacle such that no one agrees to act as wakeel. Similarly, if a debtor left the country and has cash in the country or that. In such places, if one provides proof against the absentee such that the judge's heart is reassured and his dominant opinion is that it is true, no forgery and no trickery, then he should judge for and against the absentee. Likewise, the mufti may give fatwa on its permissibility to repel hardship and necessities and protect rights from being lost, especially since it is a matter of ijtihad; al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal allowed it, and there are two narrations from our companions. The more cautious approach is to appoint a wakeel for the absentee who is known to look after the absentee's interests and not neglect his rights, so he appoints the most suitable, etc. And Allah knows best. And he confirmed it in Nur al-'Ayn Islah Jami' al-Fusulayn. His saying: 'Then it appeared to me, etc.' Al-Ramli said: Specialization to the missing person does not appear in their words; rather, the apparent meaning is general. Then, if hardship and necessity are considered, it is necessary to consider the impossibility of reaching the absentee and bringing him, such that if it is possible, it is not valid due to lack of necessity.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion by providing practical guidance. The author, citing al-Qunyah, distinguishes between the permissibility of initiating a judgment (hull al-aqdam) and the execution of that judgment (nufudh). While Hanafis generally do not allow initiating judgment on an absentee without a representative, if such a judgment is passed by a judge who holds it valid (e.g., a Shafi'i judge), it is executed without disagreement. The passage then gives examples of hardship: a missing husband who divorced his wife, or a debtor who is absent. In such cases, if evidence is strong and the judge is confident of its truth, he may judge against the absentee to prevent loss of rights, following the opinion of the majority of imams (Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad). However, the more cautious (ahwat) approach is to appoint a representative (wakil) for the absentee. Al-Ramli clarifies that this is not limited to missing persons but applies generally when hardship and necessity justify it, but only if the absentee cannot be reached; otherwise, absence of necessity renders the judgment invalid.

Key Terms
الحرج (al-ḥaraj): Hardship or difficulty that makes a legal ruling flexible.
الضرورة (al-ḍarūrah): Necessity that permits what is normally prohibited to prevent harm.
الإقدام (al-iqdām): Initiation of the legal case by the judge.
النفاذ (al-nufūdh): Execution or enforcement of the judgment.
الاحتياط (al-iḥtiyāṭ): The cautious approach, e.g., appointing a wakil.

Key Takeaway
Absentee judgment is normally prohibited in Hanafi law, but hardship and necessity can make it permissible to protect rights, with the cautious alternative of appointing a representative.

Judging Against an Absent Person: Initiation vs Execution
Inter-madhhab dispute on judging absent persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the permissibility of initiating a ruling against an absent person and the validity of its execution, and explain the Hanafi position in light of the Shafi'i disagreement.

Core Idea
A Hanafi judge should not initiate it, but if he does, the ruling is executed.

The issue of judging against an absent person (al-qada' 'ala al-gha'ib) is a classic inter-madhhab dispute. While the Shafi'i school permits it outright, the Hanafi school distinguishes sharply between the permissibility of initiating such a ruling and the binding force of the ruling once issued. This lesson unpacks that distinction and explores how the Hanafi school navigates necessity and hardship, especially in the case of a missing person (al-mafqud).

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of contention
State clearly what the dispute is about: whether a judge may issue a ruling against a defendant who is not present in court. Identify the two sides: Hanafi (cautious prohibition) and Shafi'i (permissibility).
2
Distinguish initiation from execution
The Hanafi school uses a key distinction: 'hull al-iqdam' (permissibility of initiating the ruling) vs 'nufudh' (execution of the ruling after it is given). The disagreement with Shafi'i is only on initiation, not on execution. Once a ruling is given, it is executed by consensus.
This distinction is crucial for understanding later Hanafi fatwa flexibility.
3
Analyze the special case of the missing person
The Hanafi school grants judges broader authority over the property of a missing person (mafqud) because he is treated like a deceased person. This is a key exception to the general prohibition on judging against absent persons. Contrast with an ordinary absent person who is not missing.
The missing person is not a litigant who can defend himself; the judge acts as a guardian.
4
Examine the role of necessity and hardship
Later Hanafi scholars like Ibn Nujaym and al-Ramli allow judging against the absent in cases of hardship (haraj) and necessity (darurah), such as when the absent person cannot be brought to court or when a wife is left without maintenance. The mufti may give a fatwa of permissibility to protect rights.
This flexibility is based on the principle of 'avoiding hardship' and is a later development in the mutakhkhirin tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قال الرملي : لا يظهر التخصيص بالمفقود في كلامهم بل الظاهر التعميم، ثم إذا لوحظ الحرج والضرورة يجب اعتبار عدم مراجعة الغائب وإحضاره حتى لو أمكن لا يصح لعدم الضرورة، في عدم ذلك أطلق كلامهم أن المذهب عن أصحابنا عدم صحة القضاء على الغائب وأن القاضي الذي يراه إن قضى عليه فإنه يتوقف على الإمضاء لأن الاختلاف في نفس القضاء، وما عدا هذا من الأقوال من تصرفات بعض المشايخ . ثم ظهر لي بحمد الله ما يجب المصير إليه وهو أنهم إنما قالوا بأن الفتوى على النفاذ فيما إذا قضى على مفقود لا في مطلق الغائب، ويدل على الفرق بين المفقود وغيره ما في فتاوى قاضيخان من باب فصل القضاء في المجتهدات : رجل قدم رجلاً إلى قاض وقال إن لأبي على هذا الرجل ألف درهم وأبي غائب وإني أخاف أن يتوارى هذا الرجل فجعله القاضي وكيلاً لأبيه وقبل بينة الابن على المال وحكم بذلك، ثم رفع . إلى قاض آخر فإن الثاني لا يجيز قضاء الأوّل لأن بينة الابن ما قامت بحق على الغائب حتى يكون القضاء على الغائب وإنما قامت لغائب، وهذا بخلاف المفقود إذا أقام القاضي ابنه وكيلاً في طلب حقوقه لأن المفقود بمنزلة الميت فكان للقاضي التصرف في ماله ا ه . القضاء عليه وهو مقيد بما إذا ثبت الحق ببينة سواء كان غائباً وقت الشهادة أو غاب بعدها قبل التزكية، وسواء كان غائباً عن المجلس حاضراً في البلد أو غائباً عن البلد، وأما إذا أقر عند القاضي فغاب قبل أن يقضي عليه قضى عليه وهو غائب لأن له أن يطعن في البينة دون الإقرار، ولأن القضاء بالإقرار قضاء إعانة، وإذا نفذ القاضي إقراره سلم إلى المدعي حقه عيناً كان أو ديناً أو عقاراً إلا أن في الدين يسلم إليه جنس حقه إذا وجد في يد من يكون مقراً بأنه مال الغائب المقر ولا يبيع في ذلك العروض والعقار لأن البيع قضاء على الغائب فلا يجوز ; كذا في شرح الزيادات للعتابي والإخبار بالقضاء منه كالإنشاء لا بد له من الحضرة. قال في شهادات القنية : أشهد القاضي شهوداً أني حكمت لفلان على فلان بكذا فهو إشهاد باطل والحضور شرط. وقال قبله : خرج الحاكم عن المحكمة ثم أشهد على حكمه يصح إشهاده ا ه . وفي تهذيب القلانسي : إذا قال القاضي حكمت على فلان بكذا وهو غائب لم يصدق ا ه . وقلنا على غير خصم حاضر لإخراج ما لو قضى على حاضر ليس بخصم وعلى خصم غائب فالخصم من تسمع الدعوى عليه بانفراده شرعاً، فخرج ما لو قضى على راهن في غيبة مرتهن وعكسه، وكذا في المؤجر مع المستأجر والمعير مع المستعير والموصى له ليس بخصم إلا في إثبات الوصاية أو الوكالة وغريم الميت ليس بخصم لمدعي الدين على الميت إنما الخصم وارث أو وصي وأحد الورثة خصم عن الباقي فيما للميت وما فرع قاضيخان لا يدل على المدعي تأمل قوله : (لأن المفقود بمنزلة الميت فكان للقاضي تصرف في ماله قال الرملي : وقد كثر في كلامهم للقاضي بسوطة يد في مال المفقود ما ليس في مال الغائب قوله: (وقال قبله خرج الحاكم عن المحكمة الخ قال الرملي لا يخفى أن هذا لا يلائم مذهب المتأخرين القائلين بأن علم القاضي غير معتبر فتأمل
Al-Sadr al-Shahid in Sharh Adab al-Qada said: If it were general, it would necessitate demolishing the madhhab of our companions. I am astonished at al-Bazzazi where he said in al-Fatawa: Regarding the missing person, should the judge appoint an agent over the absent person and from the absent person? According to us, he does not do so. But if he did, by ruling against the absent person, it would be executed by consensus, because the mujtahid is a cause as to whether the evidence is a proof without a present litigant for the judgment or not; so if he considers it a proof and judges, it is executed. That is the ruling, as if he judged by the testimony of sinners, and upon it is the fatwa. Then his claim of consensus is not correct, and he was preceded in this by Khwaharzadeh. In his statement 'so if he considers it a proof' is an indication that he is among those who hold the view of judging against the absent, so the imitating Hanafi is excluded. The scholar Mahmud spoke the truth when he said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: Their views and explanations have become confused in the matters of judging for the absent and against him, and they have not described nor transmitted from them a strong apparent principle on which the branches can be built without confusion or difficulty. So in my view, one should examine the situations, be cautious, and observe hardship and necessities, and then give fatwa accordingly, whether permissibility or invalidity. What appears to me from Qunyah is: The judge may not rule for separation due to inability to provide maintenance. And he himself answered repeatedly regarding someone who was absent from his wife and left her without maintenance that if he ruled for separation due to inability to provide maintenance, it is executed. He said: I only distinguish between the two answers because the disagreement between us and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) is regarding the permissibility of initiating the judgment; in his view it is permissible, and in our view it is not permissible, and there is no disagreement about execution. So the first answer is about initiation, and the second about execution with the prohibition of initiation. And it is not required that the judge be a Shafi'i in madhhab because there is no disagreement about the execution of the judgment. So it is, as you see, explicit that it is general. And his statement later after three folios, and their distinction between a cause and the cause and condition, is the clearest evidence that their statement about execution of judgment against the absent in the more apparent of the two narrations is only regarding the judgment of a Shafi'i. As for the Hanafi, no, because then there would be no meaning for the mentioned distinction. It is refuted by what preceded about the disagreement on initiating the judgment. So reflect on his statement: 'his claim of consensus is not correct' i.e., due to what was mentioned that the fatwa is on non-execution, but it was also mentioned that the fatwa is on execution and al-Bazzazi proceeded upon it in what came before, so his speech here is based on it. Reflect on his statement: 'so the apparent to me is to reflect...' The complete expression: For example, if a man divorced his wife in the presence of the registrar and then was absent from the town and his location is unknown, or known but he is unable to bring him, or she cannot travel to him, or his agent is distant, or for another impediment such that no one accepts agency, and similarly the debtor if he was absent from the town and he has cash in the town or the like. In such cases, if evidence is proven against the absent person such that the judge's heart is at ease and his dominant belief is that it is true, not fabricated, and there is no trick in it, then he should judge against the absent and for the absent. Similarly, the mufti may give a fatwa of its permissibility to avoid hardship and necessities and to protect rights from loss, noting that it is a matter of ijtihad. Al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal deemed it permissible, and there are two narrations from our companions. The most precautionary is that he appoint an agent for the absent who is known to look after the interests of the absent and not be negligent. He appoints the best then the best, and Allah knows best. And it was affirmed in Nur al-Ayn and Islah Jami' al-Fusulayn. His statement: 'then it appeared to me...' said al-Ramli: The specification to the missing person does not appear in their words; rather, the apparent is generalization. Then, if hardship and necessity are considered, it is obligatory to consider the impossibility of contacting the absent person and bringing him, such that if it is possible, it is not valid due to lack of necessity. In the absence of that, their statements are absolute that the madhhab of our companions is the invalidity of judging against the absent person, and that the judge who sees it, if he judges, then it is suspended upon confirmation because the disagreement is in the ruling itself. Apart from this, the statements are from the actions of some shaykhs. Then it appeared to me, by Allah's praise, that which must be adopted, which is that they only said that the fatwa is on execution if he judged against a missing person, not in the case of an absolute absent person. The difference between the missing and others is evidenced by what is in Fatawa Qadikhan from the chapter on judging in ijtihad matters: A man brought a man to a judge and said, 'My father has a claim of a thousand dirhams against this man, and my father is absent, and I fear that this man will hide.' So the judge appointed him as an agent for his father and accepted the son's evidence regarding the property and judged accordingly. Then the matter was raised to another judge, and the second judge did not validate the judgment of the first because the son's evidence did not establish a right against the absent person such that the judgment would be against the absent; rather, it was established for an absent person. This is unlike the missing person if the judge appoints his own son as an agent in seeking his rights, because the missing person is treated as dead, so the judge has authority to dispose of his property. So judging against him is restricted to when the right is established by evidence, whether the person was absent at the time of testimony or became absent after it before tazkiyah, and whether he is absent from the court but present in the town or absent from the town. But if he confessed before the judge and then was absent before the judge ruled, he judges against him while he is absent because he can challenge the evidence but not the confession, and because judging by confession is a judgment of aid. When the judge executes his confession, he hands over to the plaintiff his right, whether it is property, a debt, or real estate, except that in debt, he hands over its like if it is found in the hands of someone who acknowledges that it is the absent confessor's property. He may not sell goods or real estate because selling is a judgment against the absent and thus not permissible. This is in Sharh al-Ziyadat for al-'Attabi. And the report of the judgment from him is like the creation; it requires presence. He said in Shahadat al-Qunyah: If the judge bears witness to the witnesses that I have ruled for so-and-so against so-and-so for such, it is an invalid attestation and presence is a condition. And he said before: If the judge left the courtroom and then bears witness to his judgment, his attestation is valid. And in Tahdhib al-Qalanisi: If the judge said, 'I ruled against so-and-so for such,' while he is absent, he is not believed. And we said 'against someone other than a present litigant' to exclude the case where he judged against a present person who is not a litigant, and against an absent litigant. The litigant is the one against whom the lawsuit is heard individually according to the Shari'a. Thus excluded is the case where a judge rules against a pawnbroker in the absence of the mortgagee, and vice versa. Similarly, the lessor with the lessee, the lender with the borrower, the legatee is not a litigant except in proving execution of a will or agency. The creditor of the deceased is not a litigant for someone claiming a debt against the deceased; rather, the litigant is the heir or executor. One heir is a litigant for the rest regarding what is for the deceased and what is against him. The subsidiary of Qadikhan does not indicate the plaintiff. Reflect on his statement: 'because the missing person is treated as dead, so the judge has authority to dispose of his property.' Al-Ramli said: It occurs often in their statements that the judge has broad authority over the property of the missing person that he does not have over the property of the absent. His statement: 'and he said before: if the judge left the courtroom...' Al-Ramli said: It is clear that this is not consonant with the madhhab of the later scholars who hold that the judge's knowledge is not considered. So reflect.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the complex issue of a judge issuing a ruling against an absent person (al-qada' 'ala al-gha'ib). It is a dispute involving different schools and also different opinions within the Hanafi madhhab. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, begins by critiquing al-Bazzazi's claim that judging against an absent person is invalid by consensus. He points out that earlier scholars like Khwaharzadeh had already noted the claim is baseless. The discussion centers on whether a judge can initiate a judgment against someone not present in court. Al-Shafi'i permits it, while the Hanafi school generally prohibits initiation but acknowledges that if a judge does so, the judgment is executed (nufudh). The key distinction is between the permissibility of initiating (hull al-iqdam) and the validity of execution (al-nufudh). The commentator then brings in the view of Mahmud from Jami' al-Fusulayn, who advises case-by-case examination considering hardship (haraj) and necessity (darurat). Later, the commentator distinguishes between a missing person (mafqud) and an ordinary absent person (gha'ib). Citing Fatawa Qadikhan, he explains that a judge has broader authority over the property of a missing person because he is treated as dead, allowing the judge to appoint an agent to protect his rights. For an ordinary absent person, the judge may not directly judge against him unless there is a confession (iqrar) because confession is an act of aid (qada' i'anah). The passage also discusses conditions for judging against the absent: the right must be established by evidence (bayyinah) or confession, and the judge must not be a mere imitator. Finally, it notes that according to later scholars, the judge's personal knowledge is not considered, which creates some tension with earlier rulings.

Key Terms
القضاء على الغائب (al-qada' 'ala al-gha'ib): A judge's ruling against a person who is not present in court at the time of proceedings.
المفقود (al-mafqud): A missing person whose whereabouts are unknown and who has been absent for a prolonged period, considered similar to a deceased person in some legal aspects.
النفاذ (al-nufudh): The execution or enforcement of a court's ruling.
حل الإقدام (hull al-iqdam): The permissibility of initiating the judicial proceeding against an absent person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a judge issuing a ruling against an absent person (al-qada' 'ala al-gha'ib)?
A) It is absolutely prohibited and invalid.
B) It is permissible and encouraged.
C) The judge should not initiate it, but if he does, the ruling is executed.
D) It is valid only if the absent person is a missing person (mafqud).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the permissibility of initiating a judgment against an absent person and the binding force of the judgment once issued; the ruling is executed even if initiation was discouraged.

Ruling on Judgment Against an Absent Person: Distinction Between Ghā'ib and Mafqūd
States Hanafi ruling and distinction between ghā'ib and mafqūd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on judgments against absent persons, distinguish between a ghā'ib (absent known) and a mafqūd (missing), and apply the fatwa of Qadikhan to determine validity.

Core Idea
Judgment against an absent person is suspended until ratified; a missing person is treated as deceased.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq addresses a critical distinction in Hanafi judicial procedure: the difference between a ghā'ib (absent but known whereabouts) and a mafqūd (missing, presumed dead). The default position of the school is that a judgment against an absent person is not immediately valid; it is suspended (mu'allaq) pending ratification by the same or another judge. However, the author clarifies that this rule does not apply blanketly—the fatwa permits enforcement when the absent party is a mafqūd, because he is legally akin to a deceased person. The proof comes from a fatwa of Qadikhan, which illustrates the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default Hanafi position
The text states that the madhhab of the Sahibayn holds judgment against an absent person to be invalid and suspended (mu'allaq) pending ratification.
Note the term 'mu'allaq': it means the judgment is not yet binding.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites the fatwa of Qadikhan: a son acted as agent for his absent father, the judge accepted evidence and ruled; another judge invalidated it because the evidence was for the absent, not against him.
Focus on the phrase 'بينة الابن ما قامت بحق على الغائب'.
3
Extract the distinction
The key difference: for a mafqūd (missing), the judge can dispose of his wealth as if he were dead, so the judgment is valid without ratification. For a ghā'ib (known absent), the judgment requires ratification.
The missing person's legal status triggers this exception.
4
Note the conditions
The ruling applies when the right is proven by evidence, regardless of when absence occurred or location.
The condition is that the right must be established by bayyinah.
5
Contrast with other schools
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) generally allow judgment against absent persons, but Hanafi maintains the stricter view.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences in court procedures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحوالة باب كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي وغيره في عدم ذلك أطلق كلامهم أن المذهب عن أصحابنا عدم صحة القضاء على الغائب وأن القاضي الذي يراه إن قضى عليه فإنه يتوقف على الإمضاء لأن الاختلاف في نفس القضاء، وما عدا هذا من الأقوال من تصرفات بعض المشايخ . ثم ظهر لي بحمد الله ما يجب المصير إليه وهو أنهم إنما قالوا بأن الفتوى على النفاذ فيما إذا قضى على مفقود لا في مطلق الغائب، ويدل على الفرق بين المفقود وغيره ما في فتاوى قاضيخان من باب فصل القضاء في المجتهدات : رجل قدم رجلاً إلى قاض وقال إن لأبي على هذا الرجل ألف درهم وأبي غائب وإني أخاف أن يتوارى هذا الرجل فجعله القاضي وكيلاً لأبيه وقبل بينة الابن على المال وحكم بذلك، ثم رفع . إلى قاض آخر فإن الثاني لا يجيز قضاء الأوّل لأن بينة الابن ما قامت بحق على الغائب حتى يكون القضاء على الغائب وإنما قامت لغائب، وهذا بخلاف المفقود إذا أقام القاضي ابنه وكيلاً في طلب حقوقه لأن المفقود بمنزلة الميت فكان للقاضي التصرف في ماله ا هـ . القضاء عليه وهو مقيد بما إذا ثبت الحق ببينة سواء كان غائباً وقت الشهادة أو غاب بعدها قبل التزكية، وسواء كان غائباً عن المجلس حاضراً في البلد أو غائباً عن البلد
Book of Hawala, Chapter of the Judge's Letter to Another Judge and Others. Regarding the invalidity of that: Their words indicate that the school of our companions is the invalidity of judgment against the absent person, and that the judge who sees him, if he judges against him, then it is suspended pending confirmation because the disagreement is in the judgment itself. Apart from this, the statements are from the actions of some shaykhs. Then it became clear to me, by the grace of God, what must be adopted: that they only said that the fatwa is on enforcement when he judged against a missing person, not in the absolute absent person. The difference between the missing and others is indicated in the fatwas of Qadikhan, from the chapter of ruling in ijtihad: A man brought another man to a judge and said: 'My father has a thousand dirhams from this man, and my father is absent, and I fear that this man might disappear.' So the judge made him an agent for his father, accepted the son's evidence regarding the money, and ruled accordingly. Then it was raised to another judge: the second does not validate the judgment of the first, because the son's evidence was not established as a right against the absent person such that the judgment would be against the absent; rather, it was established for an absent person. This is unlike the missing person: if the judge makes his son an agent to seek his rights, because the missing person is like a dead person, so the judge has authority to dispose of his wealth. End. Judgment against him is restricted to when the right is established by evidence, whether he was absent at the time of testimony or became absent after it before verification (tazkiya), and whether he is absent from the session but present in the city or absent from the city.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage addresses the Hanafi ruling on a judge's decision made in the absence of the defendant. The author begins by stating that the established madhhab position is that such a judgment is not valid and requires ratification by another judge, because the dispute lies in the judgment itself. He then clarifies a key distinction: this rule applies specifically to a missing person (مفقود) — one whose whereabouts are unknown and presumed dead — not to an ordinary absent person (غائب). To support this, he cites a fatwa from Qadikhan: a son acted as agent for his absent father and produced witnesses; the judge ruled in favor of the absent father. When reviewed by a second judge, it was not upheld because the evidence was for the absent person, not against him. In contrast, a missing person is treated like a deceased person, so the judge can manage his affairs without the same restriction. The ruling also specifies that a judgment against an absent person is conditional on the right being proven by evidence, regardless of when the absence occurred or whether the person is absent from the court or the city.

Key Terms
الغائب (al-ghā'ib): An absent person whose whereabouts are known and who is not presumed dead.
المفقود (al-mafqūd): A missing person whose whereabouts are unknown and who is presumed dead by judicial order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is a judgment against an absent person (ghā'ib) considered valid without ratification?
A) If the absent person is present in the city.
B) If the absent person is a missing person (mafqūd).
C) If the absent person has appointed an agent.
D) If the evidence is against the absent person.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a judgment against an absent person (ghā'ib) is suspended until ratified, but a judgment against a missing person (mafqūd) is valid without ratification.
