Judgment by Confession of an Absent Person
Ruling on judgment by confession when the confessor becomes absent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a person confesses before a judge and then becomes absent, and apply the limitation that the judge cannot sell property.

Core Idea
A judge can rule based on an absent confessor's binding admission, but cannot sell property.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the scenario where a person confesses before a judge and then leaves. Despite the absence, the judge may enforce the confession and hand over the right to the plaintiff, because the confessor can only challenge witnesses, not his own confession. However, the judge cannot sell any property, as that would be a new judgment against an absent person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person confesses before the judge, then becomes absent before judgment is passed.
The confession is made in court.
2
State the ruling
The judge can still rule against the absent confessor and enforce the confession.
The judgment is valid and binding.
3
Explain the rationale
Judgment by confession is called 'qada' i'ana' (judgment of assistance); the confessor cannot challenge his own admission.
Unlike witnesses, confession cannot be questioned by the confessor.
4
Apply the limitation
The judge hands over the right (cash, debt, or real estate) but cannot sell property.
Selling would be a new judgment against an absent person, which is impermissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا أقر عند القاضي فغاب قبل أن يقضي عليه قضى عليه وهو غائب لأن له أن يطعن في البينة دون الإقرار، ولأن القضاء بالإقرار قضاء إعانة، وإذا نفذ القاضي إقراره سلم إلى المدعي حقه عيناً كان أو ديناً أو عقاراً إلا أن في الدين يسلم إليه جنس حقه إذا وجد في يد من يكون مقراً بأنه مال الغائب المقر ولا يبيع في ذلك العروض والعقار لأن البيع قضاء على الغائب فلا يجوز ؛ كذا في شرح الزيادات للعتابي والإخبار بالقضاء منه كالإنشاء لا بد له من الحضرة. قال في شهادات القنية : أشهد القاضي شهوداً أني حكمت لفلان على فلان بكذا فهو إشهاد باطل والحضور شرط. وقال قبله : خرج الحاكم عن المحكمة ثم أشهد على حكمه يصح إشهاده ا هـ . وفي تهذيب القلانسي : إذا قال القاضي حكمت على فلان بكذا وهو غائب لم يصدق ا هـ
As for when he confesses before the judge and then becomes absent before he judges against him, he judges against him while he is absent, because he can challenge the evidence but not the confession, and because judgment by confession is a judgment of assistance. When the judge enforces his confession, he hands over to the plaintiff his right, whether it is an 'ayn, a debt, or real estate, except that in the case of a debt, he hands over the species of his right if it is found in the hand of someone who admits that it is the property of the absent confessor. He does not sell the movable goods and real estate because selling is a judgment against the absent person, which is not permissible; as in Sharh al-Ziyadat by al-Utabi. And informing of the judgment from him is like establishing; it must have [the party's] presence. It is said in Shahadat al-Qunyah: The judge made witnesses testify that 'I have ruled for so-and-so against so-and-so such-and-such' — this is an invalid attestation; presence is a condition. And before that: The judge left the courthouse and then attested to his judgment — his attestation is valid. End. And in Tahdhib al-Qalanisi: If the judge says 'I judged against so-and-so such-and-such' while he is absent, he is not believed. End.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage covers two related points. First, if a person confesses to a debt before the judge and then becomes absent, the judge can still pass judgment based on that confession, because the confessor can challenge witnesses but not his own confession — it is a judgment of assistance (qada' i'ana). The judge hands over the right to the plaintiff, but if it is a debt, he only hands over the specific type of money if found in the hand of someone who admits it belongs to the absent confessor. He cannot sell movable or immovable property because that would be a new judgment against the absent person. Second, the passage addresses the attestation of judgment: informing someone of a judgment is like establishing it, and it requires the presence of the party. Citing al-Qunyah, if a judge says 'I have ruled for X against Y' in front of witnesses without the party being present, the attestation is invalid. However, if the judge leaves the courthouse and then attests, it is valid. Tahdhib al-Qalanisi adds that if the judge claims to have judged against an absent person, he is not believed.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrār): A confession made before a judge; it is a binding admission that can be enforced even if the confessor becomes absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person confesses before a judge and then becomes absent, can the judge rule based on that confession?
A) No, because the defendant must be present.
B) Yes, because the confession is binding and cannot be challenged like evidence.
C) Yes, only if the confession was in writing.
D) No, because judgment requires both parties to be present.

Key Takeaway
A judge can enforce a confession made in court even after the confessor disappears, but he cannot sell property to satisfy the claim.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Attestation of Judgment Requires Presence of the Party
Ruling on attestation of judgment and the requirement of presence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition for valid attestation of judgment and distinguish between valid and invalid attestation scenarios.

Core Idea
Attestation of judgment requires the presence of the party, except when the judge leaves the courthouse.

The second part of the passage addresses the attestation (ishhad) of a judicial decision. It clarifies that if a judge informs witnesses of his ruling without the presence of the party against whom the ruling is made, the attestation is invalid. However, if the judge leaves the courthouse and then attests, it is valid. This distinction highlights the importance of presence for the validity of the attestation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The judge attesting to his judgment by informing witnesses.
This is termed 'ishhad'.
2
State the condition for validity
Presence of the party (gharim) is required for valid attestation in court.
The text says 'al-hudur shart'.
3
Apply the condition
If the judge says 'I ruled for X against Y' in court without Y present, attestation is invalid.
The testimony is not accepted.
4
Note the exception
If the judge leaves the courthouse and then attests, it is valid even without the party present.
Location matters: inside court requires presence, outside does not.
5
Understand the principle
Attestation is like establishing a new judgment; inside court, the party must be present to hear it.
Outside court, the judge's statement is independent of the courtroom setting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا أقر عند القاضي فغاب قبل أن يقضي عليه قضى عليه وهو غائب لأن له أن يطعن في البينة دون الإقرار، ولأن القضاء بالإقرار قضاء إعانة، وإذا نفذ القاضي إقراره سلم إلى المدعي حقه عيناً كان أو ديناً أو عقاراً إلا أن في الدين يسلم إليه جنس حقه إذا وجد في يد من يكون مقراً بأنه مال الغائب المقر ولا يبيع في ذلك العروض والعقار لأن البيع قضاء على الغائب فلا يجوز ؛ كذا في شرح الزيادات للعتابي والإخبار بالقضاء منه كالإنشاء لا بد له من الحضرة. قال في شهادات القنية : أشهد القاضي شهوداً أني حكمت لفلان على فلان بكذا فهو إشهاد باطل والحضور شرط. وقال قبله : خرج الحاكم عن المحكمة ثم أشهد على حكمه يصح إشهاده ا هـ . وفي تهذيب القلانسي : إذا قال القاضي حكمت على فلان بكذا وهو غائب لم يصدق ا هـ
As for when he confesses before the judge and then becomes absent before he judges against him, he judges against him while he is absent, because he can challenge the evidence but not the confession, and because judgment by confession is a judgment of assistance. When the judge enforces his confession, he hands over to the plaintiff his right, whether it is an 'ayn, a debt, or real estate, except that in the case of a debt, he hands over the species of his right if it is found in the hand of someone who admits that it is the property of the absent confessor. He does not sell the movable goods and real estate because selling is a judgment against the absent person, which is not permissible; as in Sharh al-Ziyadat by al-Utabi. And informing of the judgment from him is like establishing; it must have [the party's] presence. It is said in Shahadat al-Qunyah: The judge made witnesses testify that 'I have ruled for so-and-so against so-and-so such-and-such' — this is an invalid attestation; presence is a condition. And before that: The judge left the courthouse and then attested to his judgment — his attestation is valid. End. And in Tahdhib al-Qalanisi: If the judge says 'I judged against so-and-so such-and-such' while he is absent, he is not believed. End.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage covers two related points. First, if a person confesses to a debt before the judge and then becomes absent, the judge can still pass judgment based on that confession, because the confessor can challenge witnesses but not his own confession — it is a judgment of assistance (qada' i'ana). The judge hands over the right to the plaintiff, but if it is a debt, he only hands over the specific type of money if found in the hand of someone who admits it belongs to the absent confessor. He cannot sell movable or immovable property because that would be a new judgment against the absent person. Second, the passage addresses the attestation of judgment: informing someone of a judgment is like establishing it, and it requires the presence of the party. Citing al-Qunyah, if a judge says 'I have ruled for X against Y' in front of witnesses without the party being present, the attestation is invalid. However, if the judge leaves the courthouse and then attests, it is valid. Tahdhib al-Qalanisi adds that if the judge claims to have judged against an absent person, he is not believed.

Key Terms
الإشهاد (al-ishhād): The act of having witnesses testify to a judicial decision; requires the presence of the party concerned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For a valid attestation of judgment inside the courthouse, what is required?
A) The judge must have witnesses present.
B) The party against whom judgment is passed must be present.
C) The judgment must be written down.
D) The judge must leave the courthouse.

Key Takeaway
Attestation of judgment is valid inside court only if the party is present; outside court, presence is not required.
